--- 帖子 #1 ---
I think I have found a very good strategy and was wandering if I could have some thoughts on this…. You know someone to play Devils Advocate J . I was sat down last night thinking about the daily range of the market and started to wander if there was some sort of relationship between where the market starts 00:00am gmt and where it finishes. For example if the market goes 50 points one way then how often does it retrace and how often does it carry on going for its 100-150 pip daily range. So I pulled up some daily data on the cable market and started back testing. I have now back tested to May 2006 and will carry on going but here are my rules. If the market goes 50 points in any one direction from the price it was at at midnight gmt. Then enter the trade with a 30 point limit order and a 30 point stop loss. This so far on Cable has given me 1500 points since the beginning of May. This looks good to me but am I missing something that is fundamentally or technically wrong with such an approach?

--- 帖子 #10 ---
Since your stop equals your profit target, you can do the following to have your trade lock in some profit, become a free trade, and potentially give you more profit. Simply take off half your position when your profit target is reached and move your stop to breakeven. Let your second half ride til it hits your trailing stop. Dial

--- 帖子 #17 ---
In the Vegas WB systems, Vegas has detailed information and his backtested data for the ranges for the major pairs. He specifies the probability of the pair to continue or reverse based on its current level for the day. Keep in mind the pair will only offer a probability of continuing for the day, as I think a lot of people expect it to happen 100% every day- which is obsurd. I don't have time to find the exact posting but I suggest reading through all of it to better inform yourself. I found it very helpful and the daily range idea has improved my analysis greatly. Oh yeah- and I've made some positive pips too. good luck

--- 帖子 #19 ---
Yes its as simple as that. At Midnight GMT. You look at the price action see where the price is. Then put a buy and sell order in 50 points away, with a take profit order of 30 pips and a stop loss of 30 pips..... So effectively your straddling. Then you simply wait for the market to do what its got to do. Don't get me wrong you do get loosing days but during my testing, so far the biggest draw down is 120 pips. Obvioulsy you need to at least double or even triple that to be on the safe side. Bottom line is this is like any other system you will get losses but in the long run you come up in profit. As I said I will keep testing this and tweaking it.... You guys should do the same then we can all come to a consensus in a few months time as to if this works or not and whether or not the levels need to be adjusted.

--- 帖子 #30 ---
If , once the Market has moved 50 pip it then retraces 33 pips Then the 50 is wrong Or Slide the Time Scale Slightgly There will be no 100% answer to this but this Timed Breakout Strategy {00:00 GMT, 5:00 EDT Bar Close} is playing the New York Business Day Open. Give me the Close of a Bar Before the start of the N.Y. Business Day. Watch the Currency Market to monitor how the Stocks/News are doing. Once the Pair has Indicated it is going to have a +/- day, Get me in the Currency Market. Things I should know; What's the Average Daily Range of the Pair I want to trade. 100pips? 125pips? Or maybe just 50 pips? What is the Range {DayH-DayL} Today So Far, now that I want to get in? What is the difference between those two Ranges. {How many more Pips can I reasonably expect the Pair to move?} Is this Trade worth the Risk? I think you will find that you can reduce the 50Pip Entry Trigger substantially. You may also find that Different Pairs require the Clock to start ticking at a Different Time. Is there a relationship between the Times Your Trades are Signaled? Good luck &amp; hth.

--- 帖子 #32 ---
I was looking at a strategy similar to this for the last few months. The basis of the strategy was to take the close of the hour session prior to the &lt;?xml:namespace prefix = st1 ns = "urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:smarttags" /&gt;&lt;st1:City w:st="on"&gt;&lt;st1 lace w:st="on"&gt;London&lt;/st1 lace&gt;&lt;/st1:City&gt; open. I would then add 20 Pips both ways. When the price reaches either target put in two orders. &lt;?xml:namespace prefix = o ns = "urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:office" /&gt;&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; Order one take at 14 pips&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; Order two take at 80 Pips&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; Also played around with a third order as a lot of the first move would reach around 40 pips only to retrace and come out with only 14 pips profit. Another order would take profit at 30 pips. &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; Put stop on both orders at the &lt;st1:City w:st="on"&gt;&lt;st1 lace w:st="on"&gt;London&lt;/st1 lace&gt;&lt;/st1:City&gt; open price. Once second order reaches 30 pips move to breakeven. &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; There can be choppy days and even choppy months but in the back testing I did had only one unprofitable month (August - 142 PIPS) Over 5 months this strategy gained 2302 PIPS averaged 280 approx a month. Only reason for abandoning this strategy was the need to watch the charts continually throughout the day.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt;

--- 帖子 #37 ---
The only problem I find with taking profit at 30 pips only is if it reverese prior to taking some profit and your stop loss gets hit your out 60 - 90 pips depending on the stop loss gap. What I found most of the time was that if you entered order 20 pips away from London open you would nearly always take 14 pips of the table on first order. If the trade reversed against you then you would be down 26 Pips for second and third being stopped out. If the trade continued your way then you would make a sizable profit for the day. The win reward ratio was good most of the time risking 26 pips for a maximum 114 pips win. If third order was not hit you still walked away with 44 pips. first order - 14 pips second order - 30 pips third order - 80 pips

--- 帖子 #48 ---
Just a theoretical question - with such a simple system, do you really think that the market will allow you to get away with it? I have yet to see a simple mathematical system as such that can win in the long run. What makes this system any less arbitrary than any other similar system? IS this a system that will grow capital or perhaps just keep you in for a while until you can come up with something better? IS there a distinct historical advantage to waiting for 50 pips, or even at that specific time, or is this 50 pip some kind of relation to Average True Range. How about the 30 pip target, is it just as arbitrary? Point being, these systems all have one thing in common - they are all looking for any reason to get in, or rather it would seem that they are rationalizing a reason to get in based on a false premise. There is no edge getting in after 50 pips, I believe you should just wait 5 pips, why not? The only difference is that this 50 pip barrier creates the illusion of reason. I'm not trying to knock your strategy, there are really good strategies for playing black jack out there, but these strategies will all end up in the long run with a net loss. - unless of course you have a well thought out card counting strategy that can put the edge on your side - Do you feel that this strategy gives you any kind of edge in the market? I could be wrong but progress will only occur once these and many more questions are answered.

--- 帖子 #52 ---
Micardo, I understand that this entry is based on a 2 year historical perspective, but being so, does this entry figure get adjusted to keep this perspective updated? Having used this same logic, would it have worked for the two years prior? The reason I am being so harsh about this is that what you are doing is actually making it harder for you to come up with a logical stop loss area within the context of your trade. Where is your trade no longer valid? Well, if it is an arbitrary trade, than the stop loss will probably be just as arbitrary. The market doesn't care that you do not want to risk more than 40%-60% of your potential reward and therefore your stop loss will only make sense to you and not really be a function of where the trade logic is no longer valid. I could tell you to use fibonnacci clusters to pinpoint stop loss areas as a move through these will usually indicate more to come, but what if this is too big of a risk to fit your parameters. Point being, figure out the reason for your trade other than just attempting statistical manipulation, even if you do keep the 50 pip barrier to entry. Howabout, instead of making it 50 pips, you wait for the 1st pullback after the 50 pip barrier. buy stop the high if MACD is positive or whatever momentum filter you like and set stop loss at swing low minus a few pips and set your profit target at twice that amount as long as that amount doesn't bring you over 75%-80% of the expected daily range - when I say expected daily range I say so because there are going to be days when news items are coming due and you really cant trust these breakout signals prior to it. The market is then more likely show a much lower daily range, in which case you should avoid these times altogether. And instead of making it 50 pips, howabout making it 40-50% of the 14 day Average true range? For GBP it will be in that 50-70pip range anyway, and now this is no longer an arbitrary number - it is a belief that after penetrating a certain amount of the average daily range, the market is more likely to complete that range in accord with the current direction. Not trying to change everything all of a sudden, just some ideas that might have a little bit of an adaptive value to them to keep your logic current.

--- 帖子 #54 ---
This 65% - what does it refer to - the direction continuing? or does it refer to that price will move up 30 pips in your direction before moving thirty pips in the opposite direction. Does this 30 pips include the spread in these statistics? This could make a big difference. 4 pips less on the win versus 4 pips more on the loss now makes your risk/reward 17/13 as aopposed to 1/1. At 65% profitable trades, your expected gain per lot after 100 trades is 250 pips. at 56% profitable, that becomes a 20 pip loss. That my friend is a difference of 9 trades per hundred, and its not accounting for any kind of slippage. at 50% profitable, you are getting killed, which with arbitrary systems, I believe that is really what you are looking at once enough data is used in backtesting. Now think of that total system risk in terms of total system rewards, You are risking at 50% profitable, losing 200 pips per 100 trades not including slippage or any other outside circumstances that can affect you. If you are 100% correct, you can expect 250 pips in 100 trades. If you are somewhere in between you will most likely break even or lose money in 100 trades, if taken daily, basically 100 trading days or 5 months. If used with leverage, you could really get wiped out. - This all not including the possible enormous drawdowns that occur with basic coin flip strategies. I'm not saying it doesn't work, but you better be 95% certain of your edge and be constantly evaluating it, and not stray one inch from the strategy in order to make it profitable.

--- 帖子 #55 ---
This strategy has definetly been profitable over the last five months that I tested it. What I found was to set your entry from the London open price as between 12am and 6am just seems not to be the true direction of the market in most cases. Setting an entry 20 pips from market open seemed to work best. This strategy means that you could also be into a trade up to 6 times a day if market was choppy. Some choopy days proved not to be profiatable while others where. On choppy days the 3rd order would not get hit but the profit 1 at 14 and profit 2 30 pips where reguly hit and sometimes 3 - 4 times through the day. With this system you try to maintain your account through the choppy days and live for the day when the move goes one way and you collect all 3 profits. The first profit of 14 pips is a good level as it seems to help minimize you loses when market moves against your trade. First profit is almost always hit once price moves 20 pips above London open. Llambert 3 These were my entry rule: Draw line 1 - 6am close Draw line 2 - 6am close + 20 Pips Draw line 3 - 6am close - 20 Pips Buy 3 lots when line 2 is hit Stop loss 6am close take 1 lot 14 pips take 2nd lot 30 pips set 3rd lot to breakeven take 3rd lot 80 pips Reverse for the sell Sell line 3 stop loss 6am close take 1 lot 14 pips take 2nd lot 30 pips set 3rd lot to breakeven take 3rd lot 80 pips close all orders NY close If you want to see the good months and bads months and try to design a filter then run these rules manually through May for a good month and August for a bad month. Regarding % of 14 pips 1st target hit? my original target was for ten pips but changed to 4 pips to cover spread. I would say 80 - 90 % first profit is hit. If trade reverses against you after 1st profit taken then trade loss is 30 pips + spread but reward is 125 pips if full profit is taken. You also need to hit 30 pips for a sure win of 44 pips. Cheers

Mikejody, I dont have any problems with the strategy nor with the fact that you cant watch it all day and night. However do not say that statistical probability strategies work as well as any other trading strategy. Maybe as well as any other unverifiable statistical strategies. You have tested this strategy over a two year filter - making intraday trades based on a two year filter. Just to put things in perspective statistically, 3 years of hourly backtesting is equivalent to about 80 years of daily backtesting. Where is your population or your sample? 2 years? Are you telling me that that is what you are basing your trading on. Do you know how much marketconditions can change? You get annoyed with me for posing these questions and that is ok, I will stop asking, but please do not confuse my intentions. Overanalysis can lead to paralysis, but making that claim when you are trying to come up with a "statistically probable strategy" is very contradictory - your whole system is based on statistical analysis for christs sake! Avoid the analysis or over analysis or whatever you want to call it and all you have is a couple of guys trying to cheat the market and themselves by rationalizing reasons as to why they should avoid questions that put their strategies whole logical basis at risk. These and many more questions should be answered! However, if all you want is a reason to jump right in, hey go for it, but don't start a thread, just do it. I'll be waiting patiently on the other side. I am amazed by all of you! You try to statistically manipulate this market, forgetting how many market participants exist, how many are trying to do exactly what you are, and how many are smarter, faster, more creative, have backing, and are more disciplined. Not as an insult, but there are always smarter,faster,etc. With all of this knowledge, you fail to acknowlege one key statistic. 95% fail and Lose their money. If you dont want to be part of that one, I would seriously consider overanalyzing your statistically "probable" system. Best of Luck to you all.

--- 帖子 #95 ---
Markj, It looks like you left both sides of the straddle on for a while. Did you remove the other side at some point, like when you took profit on the final order from the first side? Also, did you figure out if it is more profitable to leave both sides on, or to remove the other side as soon as one side opened? I did some manual backtesting a few days ago with a strategy that would place a stradle 20 pips away and then simply go for 20 TP and 20 SL, and what I found was that there was absolutely no benefit in keeping both sides out there. I made exactly the same number of pips if I kept it, or if I removed it as soon as one side opened. At least that's what I was able to figure out over the last 2.5 month of data. Not sure if it would be the same with your strategy.

--- 帖子 #96 ---
Disclaimer: This is a spontaneous idea and post. If you're crazy enough to actually put real money on anything that's written by some guy on a forum, at least 1. don't blame the guy for any outcome that comes from this 2. know why you are doing. Basically I am saying this is more academic than anything. I am not responsible for what you do after reading this. --------------------- The IDIOT system Hi all and welcome to the The Interesting Daily Intricate Opening Trade System. While you might think I am trying to poke fun at you here, and I might or not be, I may have just stumbled across the most dumbfoundingly simple way to trade cable Since I am not a big man of many words, let me get right to it: At midnight in GMT+2 (or at least I think I am in GMT+2, just assume Berlins timezone), you place a straddle on cable's opening price of the 1H bar for that time. Basically should be the same as the daily close, can vary 1-2 pips. I go off 1h. The straddle goes like this: 30 pips above and below the opening price of the 1H candle/bar for midnight you put buy and sell orders in that direction(below the price short, above the price long. Don't forget to add your spread). You then put the stop at the opposite orders entry price (so roughly a 60 pip stop). You then set a limit for either 100 or 140 or 200 or 240 pips away. Or you can complicate it to heck and back with indicators and fibs, be my guest. After looking back about 4 weeks, I can safely say that if one of the two orders gets triggered, one of two things happens: 1. The trade moves 100-240+ pips in your direction and you get a good R/R on the stop size. 2. The trade moves about 10-40 pips in your favor, then comes all the way back and continues the other way. It will almost certainly move in your favor first. Obviously nobody will have issues with case 1, and for case 2 it's rather simple: use a 60 pip trailing stop, not a fixed one. That way you lose less. You can also move up the stop to breakeven if you're anal about it, but that might just stop you out of trades early that then move on quite a bit. Losing is normal and natural and hence the take profit / limit points should at least be 150% of the stop size. Hence 100 pips being the smallest suggested. Well, er, that's it. Straddle away every day, make money, make some hay. Best application of how MM and risk management works for you in application ever. I came up with this because all these indicator based systems are just making me sick sick sick and this works at least as well as any bagosidomoutekisilvertigerfireriderwaterspoutermysticrivershijiujitsutunnelaikenshiakirawhatever. Also it gets tiresome to read a new thread every day asking "where do you think GBPUSD is headed"(with this it just plainly doesn't matter). Backtest this yourself(As in manually, not automated. Just use the crosshair.) on the MT4 charts on 1h if you think it's too silly to work Should at least work until the 300+ pips a day moves return for cable and then all you need to do is toss in cash anyway Good luck and remember, we can all be IDIOTs if we just try hard enough! SeekingLight P.S. If you are one of the persons that needs a reason as to WHY this works, I can offer you that most of the time that time area makes an inside bar and basically it's a straddle of just that(which is indeed valid)...oh and if you need an MT4 demo that's in that timezone, MigFX and Nextt are. P.P.S. Included fully mechanically backtested October via template, made on MigFX demo. PL ends up +210 with a theoretical open trade at +50 atm. Just open a GBPUSD chart in MigFX demo and load the template, it's fully labeled. 60 trailing stop loss was used, 100 fixed take profit point. PL should be a bit lower due to spread not being included almost ever. Saw at least two trades that wouldn't have been entered the wrong direction had one used 35 pips + spread instead of 30 distance. Further tweaking is more usefull with an automated program that would examine standard deviation to both sides from that offset. Don't look at me, I can't do that sort of thing.

--- 帖子 #97 ---
Ikholod, I would set two 3 lot orders at London open. Lets assume the London open was 18800, set 3 lot orders to buy 18820, set 3 lot orders to sell at 18780. Lets say the first price gets to 18850 after breaking through the 18820 price. I would take profit one and two of the table and set profit three to brakeven. If the price then moves to 18854 before retracing to 18820 profit three would be closed out. If price then went done to 18780 sell orders would be place, if price moved only to 18760 then retraced to 18820 then only profit one would be collected, profit two and three would be closed out. If price then pushed back through 18820 again I would place 3 buy lot orders again. If price then reached 18900 then I would take all three profits of the table. If 3rd order was still there but hadn't reached 80 pips profit by NY close then this order would be closed for whatever profit is on the table. Result First move = 14 + 30 + 0 = + 44 Second move = + 14 - (-20) - (-20) = (- 26) Third move = 14 + 30 + 80 = 124 Total daily pips = 164 - 26 = 138 So the first orders are placed at the London open and left if both of these are hit proceeding orders are placed throughout the day if conditions are met. I my strategy I did not just take one 3 lot for the day, it could be upto 4 or 6. Hope helps Cheers

--- 帖子 #113 ---
For this situation there were two rules that I followed. 1. I would not re-open an order in the same direction on the same candle 2. I would no re-open an order in the same direction on candle prceeding the close candle I would however open a new order on the same candle or proceeding candle in the opposite direction. I found that if the above two happened the market was too indecisive. (this was just my rule) I would note that I didn't see the order hit either way and get stopped in the same candle very much. However I would get stopped and it would break in the same direction the next candle but I would take it. Sometimes in this situation it would make some profit but most times it would play around the order level and retrace. If the second candle closed below the order price and the third candle then broke the order line I would take the order. There may be a better rule to use here but this is seemed to work. Hope helps? but note sure how you would automate this rule?

Natgo, Is this your scenario? 3 profit levels, 14, 30 and 80. Scenario 1 Place order for 7 lots: 5 lots take profit 1 (14 pips) profit of = 70 2 lots take profit 2 and 3 (30 and 80 pips) = 110 Scenario 2 If trade moves against us after profit one hit : 5 lots taken profit 1 = 70 pips 2 lots closed out with 20 pips stop loss = - 40 pips Still in profit after spread cost of (70 - 40 + spread 28 = 2 pips) Scenario 3 Total loss on all 5 lots: 7 lots closed out = - 140 pips Scenario 2 would break (approx) even after you cover spread costs. If we look back and scenario 1 was hit 30% of the time, Scenario 2 60% of the time and scenario 3 10% per 100 trades. Calculation: 30 trades = scenario 1 = ((30 x (5 * 14) + (30 x 30) + (30 x 80)) = wait, get calculator (70 + 900 + 2400 = 3370) 60 trades = scenario 2 = (60 x 30 = 1800) 10 trades = scenario 3 6,7 lot profit only = (10 x 2 lots of 30 = 600) Spread cost = (100 x 7 lots = 2100) If this is the case profit comes to ((3370 + 1800) - (600 + 2100) = 5170 -2700 = 2470 spread cost is a killer. So we if we look back and see that profit 1 was hit 90% of the time once it broke through entry line without retracing to the London open price (10 - 1) trades then this should work assuming price moved to 80 pips above London open 30% of the time. I guess the good thing about range strategies are they can be simple! so we don't want to complicate this (but if it works). In the end if we were to use just one order to collect profits at 14 pips assuming 90% per 100 trades = 1400 - 300 spread cost - (10% losing trades at - 20pips = 200) = 900. I'm starting to get confused here and I wrote this. Just trying to put to paper what Natgos thought were. Hope calculations are correct (maths was not my strongest point). Cheers

--- 帖子 #160 ---
I only joined this thread in the middle of the week, so my first trade was Thursday. So far, I am doing the strategy exactly as posted in the initial posts in this thread. In other words, at days end (5:00 PM ET on my platform) I enter 2 orders. The first is a limit order to go long at + 50 pips from the close, with a take profit order of +30 (from the entry) and a stop loss of -30 (from the entry). The second order I place is to go short if the market sinks -50 pips from the close with a take profit of 30 pips and a stop loss of 30 pips. My first trade on Thursday night was profitible. The market hit + 50 so my order triggered and then hit the + 30 take profit. This is how I am trading this system, as it works best with my schedule. I hope the post is clear so that it does not spark lots of questions simply because I was too vague to clarify in the initial post.

--- 帖子 #202 ---
Here is a spreadsheet based on 21 trading days. It includes both a bear run and the current bull run. The second page may tell a story. The average open-low regardless of where the bar closed is 46. If the bar closed down, the average open-low is 60. This means if 50 pips is the limit order, on average you would only get in a trade if the bar will close down, but will not hit the 30 pips. Conversly, the average high-open is 67, regardless of where the bar closed, and if it closed up the average high-open is 87. This means a 50 pip limit order, on average, will get you in a trade even if the bar eventually closed down. These numbers, though, are very close to the 50 you guys have been talking about, and if you can get a bias, maybe put the entry at 50 pips according to your bias, and 60 pip against your bias. Any other thoughts on this is appreciated, but interesting indeed. (Sorry- One of my columns was labeled wrong before)

--- 帖子 #203 ---
Max77, This system places trades as they hit either, 20 pips below London open or 20 pips above London open. This is not a two order straddle where you set two orders at seperate points to enter trade and thats it for the day. In this systems you may enter 1,2,3, 4 or even 5 trades in a day. But normally averages around 2 - 3. I then trade 3 lots when either line is reached with 3 different profit levels. 14, 30 and 80. Today their were two trades where the price hit the uper target line (20 pips above London open) First trade at 9GMT where price went to 1.9025 and I collected 1st and 2nd profit for 44pips the 3rd lot was moved to break even when 2nd profit was collected and was closed out on the 11am candle for breakeven. Second trade would have been entered on the 1GMT time. The reason it was not entered at 12gmt time candle is that I will never re-enter a trade in the same direction on the next candle when trade has been stopped. This second trade then took all three profit levels of 14, 30 and 80 pips. Total gains for this system, this month on paper, have been 1604. Total losses have been - 730. Hope this helps Cheers

--- 帖子 #213 ---
Micardo, Great. The worst thing that I wanted to see was a confusing thread regarding 100 different ways of trading the system. But if we can pull it into line and repost to the front of the thread, then great. Don't know about you but when reading some of these thread you lose interest very quickly when the system gets so many variations that it becomes impossible to follow who is trading what and the results. Regarding the 12GMT, 1GMT entry. A rule I adapted to this system was never re-enter an order (if it has been closed out) in the same direction on the next hour candle. It is however ok to enter on 2nd candle. The reason I applied this rule is that if an order is closed out it can rebound quickly only to continue down direction the next candle. A lot of the time a order stop especially if only the 3rd profit is left has a big move so is inclined to a temp reverse. I found waiting for the 2nd candle kept you out of a lot of false rebounds. Cheers

I love Markj's strategy. I get up for like 5 minutes in the middle of the night (eastern time zone), set my entry orders with the appropriate profit targets. Of course, sitting in front of a computer anyway is very beneficial to me. I love that it can be mechanically traded though. One thing I am adding to it is moving the stop loss to lock in any profit (instead of breaking even) right before a news announcement like ISM, for example. That way in case it causes a big dip, I can keep that profit. If the news doesn't effect the pair in this way, I will put the stop loss back to breakeven, to allow the trade to breathe.

My broker has a 5 pip spread for this pair and I am trading a mini account ($1 per pip) If the 3am candle opened at 1.8800, then I'd set up a trade to buy 3 lots at 1.8820 (for simplicity let's say it is just a long trade and forget the sell)... Manul, I set my 1st profit at 14 pips. I would only add spread cost to 2nd and 3rd profit positions. The reason for this is that once price moves into 2nd and 3rd profit positions it is gaining momentum and rarley stops there so adding spread to profit target 2 and 3 will not see you miss many of these positions. However the first profit position is more fragile as market has not yet made a definite move and adding 3-5 pips onto the 1st target could see you miss a few of these positions. So if you decide to add spread to profit targets and your broker spread cost is 4 I would suggest the following: 1st Profit - 14 2nd Profit - 34 3rd Profit - 84 I am in the process of finalising some detail documentation and indicators to go with this system. I will post here when complete. Cheers

--- 帖子 #231 ---
Hey Guys ok I have varied my strategy slightly.... I found that just taking a straight 30 pips profit or 50 stop loss although profitable could definitely be improved. So The new strategy is same set up but you trade 2 lots. and 2 profit targets.... 30 pips and 80 pips. The stop loss is still 50 pips. Once the first profit target is hit you move the stop to break even and wait till second target is hit or 00:00gmt. Also I have also added the fact that you can re-enter. But only if you get stopped out before hitting your first target. If you have already hit the frst target and then get stopped out on the second lot at break even then you leave it. Results for the past 2 months are: 39 Trades 26 Wins 13 Loss Profit pips - 1924 Loss pips - 996 Total P/L: +928 for the two months. Not to bad huh :-) Ok Just waiting for Kamanda's feedback then we will get started on back testing over a period of years, and developing the EA

--- 帖子 #260 ---
Ok thanks for the feedback everybody. I just woke up so give me a few. I was so wrapped up in numbers I neglected to mention a couple of key details, and I'm sorry about that. The main one for now (while I examine the comments you guys made in further detail) is that the EA has several 'inputs' you can set--but they're hidden within the EA. I made them that way after I discovered the backtester doesn't necessarily respect inputs set directly in the code and compiled (it allows you to bypass them completely with the 'expert properties' button). For those that don't want to open the code to examine, here is the version with normal, visible inputs. The inputs include the hour (0-23) from whose previous hour close you set the base price, the hour you want to actually start setting up buys and sells (I think Markj uses the same hour for both of these-I split them out for testing/fun), the 'close' time for the day, the buy line/sell line offset from base price for each day, TP1,2,&amp;3, etc... If you change them, please make sure to observe basetime&lt;=starttime&lt;closetime and stay away from midnight until I make sure the code can handle input errors and day rollovers properly. &lt;CLOSETIME, class=inlineimg title=Smile alt="" border="0" src="http://www.forexfactory.com/forexforum/images/smilies/smile.gif" Thanks again for the feedback, I'll have more for you in just a bit! *note--LotSize is size per EACH order. eg lot size of 1 would result in 3 1.0-sized longs and 3 1.0-sized shorts. I was using 0.1 in testing. All of the Offsets/SL's/TP's are to be given in pips. eg Mark used 20 for all of BuyOffset,BuySL,SellOffset,SellSL. BuyOffset and SellOffset are pip offsets from the baseline where you want the Buy and Sell lines to go. BuySL and SellSL are offsets from the Buy and Sell line for your stoplosses. SLOffset determines where you move the third order's SL after profit of 1 and 2 are taken. 0=breakeven, 5 would lock in 5 pips profit, etc.

--- 帖子 #262 ---
Alright I'm having coffee and can address some of the feedback now. llambert3: I think most of your question is answered with being able to set your BaseTime in the inputs. Whatever hour you specify corresponds to the hour on your terminal's server. For instance, if I use 10 as BaseTime, 10:00am=8:00am London Time in my terminal...Also keep in mind your spread difference. Buys are triggered on Ask price--so for instance if your spread is 5 and your BuyOffset is 20, a buy is triggered at a BID distance of 15 from the baseline for the day. The bars you see painted in the charts are all BID prices. This is one of the reasons why I split all those variables out into inputs. Markj: Could you please include the dates/times on your charts? That way I can run the EA and physically look at the same chart you are showing and figure out what is happening. If it's easier I only need your explanation and the date. On Buy Stops always add the spread so if 5 ticks spread it should be 25 On Sell stops do not add the spread so it should be 20 This is to Open the Order for the Day For the EA After the order is entered as outlined below. For the Orginal Buy Stop putting on the Sell Stop should not add the Spread For the Orginal Sell Stop and Buy Stop should add the spread , if 5 should be 25. Input into the EA using the Spread of 5 (as an example) BuyOffset 25 BuySL 20 Sell Offset 20 Sell SL 25

I have only read about half the posts in this thread but there is one thing that no one seems to have taken into account. A lot of your trades would unintentionally turn out to be news straddles - with all the problems of no fills and slippage that goes with it. No amount of backtesting or demotesting is going to solve that problem.

--- 帖子 #276 ---
Thats what has me thinking. Really what these strategies are trying to do is place ourselves in a position such that our trades are within the body of the candle and in the direction of it. If its an up candle we're probably in a long position and vice versa if its a down candle. I take from this then that the 50 pip straddle is really to get our trades out of the irregular counter trend shadows that appear opposite the direction of the candle. i.e. a shadow above an open for a down candle and a shadow below an open in an up candle. For increased success rates all we need to do is increase the straddle. It's common to see a shadow of 1 pip in the counter trend, but is it common to see a shadow of 70+ pips? It's very common to see the candle bodies 70+ pips however. The straddle is really just a filter to filter out the counter trend and find the actual trend of the candle. A simple answer to your post would be to test out increasing the straddle from 50 to 70 pips. It would require 79 pips of movement to achieve my 5 pip goal, which is reasonable for a candle body to accomplish, but not the shadow. When we do this we are adjusting what we're willing to accept. With a 70 pip straddle we're likely to have several days where no trade is triggered. Would you rather have no trade or a losing trade though? The problem however is when we get to a 70 straddle we are making a lot more situations where the candle can stall and we're stuck with an open trade only a few pips short of it's TP. Yesterdays candle in gbp/usd is an example of this. Today might be forming the same way. It's all up for debate, but don't we have the same situation when we have the 50 pip straddle? Perhaps somewhere inbetween 50 and 70 pips is a better fit. It's all about the marginal benefit we receive from waiting for that one more pip. Where is the tipping point between filtering out bad trades at 50 pips and putting us into more situations of stalled candles at 70 pips? For SL I would probably just use a hard 20 or 30 SL. I've live traded the past two days using the 50 pip straddle and my 5 pips is usually hit within seconds of opening the trade. Trading multiple currencies like this could easily overcome a SL hit here or there which is what is expected if the probability of success really is very high in this system. Matt

Take a look at Friday the 3rd of November. On first appearances your strategy would have worked and on a demo account it probably would have worked. Have you heard of news straddling? It doesn't work! Most of your trades in this strategy turn out to be news straddles.

--- 帖子 #286 ---
Permanentjuan, I feel that if you could get your strategy to a high win percentage then excellent. A few pitfalls are and im sure you've heard this a thousand times before: 1: Yes there is enough movement easily at least in the GBP/USD market to make 5 pips a day (Average range is 140) 2: Stop loss placement is the key to this success. As with my strategy in theory when you look at a daily chart only, it cant lose. But you need to take the daily noise into account as this can often stop you out. Maybe a good strategy would be to put triggers in at London open a few pips above and below daily support and resistance. Then put you stop the opposite end. So for example... you have a buy trigger in at 5 pips above daily resistance, your stop loss for that trade should then be 5 pips below daily support. This way you are giving the trade room to breath but at the same time saying that if my buy is triggered then it retraces below the days low then I will come out as it is likely to break to the downside. I dont have the exact figure but something to this effect could work. I also trade breakouts and these are all things I consider when trading... hope this helps.

--- 帖子 #289 ---
Can someone post a chart example of how the second strategy would have traded on Friday. Unless I'm wrong, you would have been whipsawed to death that day, correct? My London open price was 1.9091. Price later hit 1.9111 on the next 1 hour bar. That would have got you long with a stop at 1.9091. Stop was hit on the next bar, so that's -20 on 3 lots (-60). You then enter short on the same bar when 1.9071 was hit. The stop on that trade was then hit at 1.9091. So that's another -20 on 3 lots (-60). Another short signal came later when 1.9071 was hit again, and went on to make +14, +30, and +80. So that's +4 for the day excluding spread.

--- 帖子 #298 ---
Pick a month and place all of your trades on charts with entry and exit price arrows in MT4. Be sure to follow the rules precisely. Save the chart as a template file and send it to your friendly EA creator along with instructions as to which broker you're using (so they can use the same platform). Also, provide a trade log in spreadsheet format. Be sure to have notes column where you can insert notes pointing out discrpancies between your manual backtests and the EA entries/exits. Also, be sure to described the precise settings you're using in the EA. That should help him/her a lot with spotting possible issues with the EA (and/or discovering inconsistencies with the strategy should they exist). Good luck!

--- 帖子 #308 ---
Yes, EST is Eastern Standard Time, also stated as Eastern Time. So, we are looking at the same time. My broker has different open prices (Tradestation) then the ones you listed. One thing I have been noticing is that Frankfurt opens an hour early, this causes early movement somedays. So, as a filter, I have been taking the close as of 1:00 AM EST (one hour before Frankfurt, two hours before London). If the price has moved more than 10 pips, I don't take the trade in that same direction. ie: If the price dropped 15 pips since 1:00 AM EST, then don't take the first sell signal. If the price breaks through the buy signal (20 pips over the London open), then take that trade. This seems to filter out some of the whipsaw. And it also seems to make the buy trade much stronger as it is on the rebound, in the above situation. Am working on making some screen shots with examples. The 14, 30, and 80 targets seem to work out pretty well. Once it breaks the 30, seems to have about a 50/50 shot of breaking 80. Otherwise it overs around the 30 mark. Not too often it drops back to the open (unless there is news involved). I did find that the 25 SL worked out a bit better too, as there would be times the price would just break the Londen Open price and rebound. David

--- 帖子 #335 ---
If the price comes back to the OPEN, you may trade at any time on the opposite side (long here) if it triggers; but if you have been stopped out on the short side whether fully stopped out or partially stopped out, you can trade on the same direction (short here) on the 2nd hourly bar of the stop-out bar, if the short is triggered again. By trigger, I mean cross of +20,-20 lines from the home line. howard

Looking back over the past 4 weeks of data I have a 22 pip straddle seems to work ok and would eliminate days like today and yesterday where it went through by just 1 pip. As I have an SB account and don't trade in lots, I'm changing the rules slightly to suit me. My first target is 20 pips above/below b/e - however after it has moved 15 above/below b/e then I will move my stop to b/e. This cuts down my losses and makes the stat's better for a SB account. Prior to moving it, my stop-loss is at 17 pips above/below the trigger (giving me a maximum 20 pip loss - 3 pip spread on GBP/USD) If the trade is triggered prior to 9.30am news then I've found the optimum get out time is around 9.35 - 9.45am. If the trade is triggered after 9.30am then look to take only 20 pips. However if it is triggered but the 20 pip target hasn't been hit before 1.30pm news, then look for 40 pip target on the news. No trades to be entered after 3pm. I've also not looked at any reversal trades, only one trade per day triggered from the 8.00am open. Over the past 4 weeks that has given me 3 losing trades and 16 winning trades and 1 breakeven trade. 360 winning pips 60 losing pips Nett pips = 300 Perhaps not as good as trading in lots, but I would still be more than happy if these results continue.

--- 帖子 #393 ---
Hello all, Anyone have any results, or at least been following along to see if this works? I'm at a new position which requires me to work 6-7 days a week so I haven't had the time. That's exactly why I want to find the solution to this system. A minute of time a day to set up the trades then walk away. Right now I'm analyzing nearly 3 years worth of data in excel to find that magical point of efficiency. I'm an economist so I'm thinking that there should not be multiple exit points. My thinking is that by having multiple exit points we're losing pips even if we hit all of our profit levels. How so? Because if we have hit all of our TP's, then we would have been better off if we had sold all of our investment at the max TP. By creating multiple TP's we are simply creating inefficiency. What we should be looking for is a point that is hit often enough to maximize our profits compared to our SL. Unfortunately the deciding factor in the success of this system is the SL. What SL is large enough to allow winning trades to stay winners while preventing us from losing 200 pips in a trade? I'm essentially asking the same question the systems are based off of. If a price moves 50 pips from the open, what're the chances it'll continue to 100? The problem is that by waiting for 50 pips we have missed much of the move and to get 50 pips would require a lot more movement in the same direction. The chances of it doing so are slim compared to the chances of the price moving only another 5 pips past 50 to 55 pips. Then the SL comes in. Our profit levels are too small to overcome the larger hits on the SL. So what we need to find is an equilibrium point to maximize profit and make it efficient. Where is our straddle? What TP will be hit enough to overcome the loss in SL hits? I'll give several examples. Out of 718 days of data in my chart, 354 are up days. There are a few I threw out because they were doji's and there are a few updays where the actual major move was down. I'm not going to confuse things further right now. I'll post those results later if I ever read through all of it correctly. So say our SL is 30 pips and our TP is only 5 to increase probability of successful trades. My straddle is 60 pips. So the number of instances where price is 60-68 are considered SL hits since my spread is 4 and I need a move of 69 to exit with 5 pip profit. There are 281 trades that would have been made on the up days with 27 of them being bad trades. (Again, many of those probably ended up as good trades on the next days candle, or could have been saved from another method but I'm keeping it simple.) So 254 good trades for a profit of 1270. On the 27 bad trades we'll assume they were worst case scenerio and they each got stopped out at 30 pips. So a loss of 810. Net profit over 281 trades is 460 pips. Now lets change our TP to 10 pips, but keep the 60 pip straddle and 30 SL. So there are still 281 trades. Anything from 60-73 is stopped out. Anything from 74+ pips is a good trade. Out of the 281 trades, 33 would be bad trades while 248 would be good. So 2480 pips in profit with 990 in loss. Total Net Profit is then +1490. Another scenerio, TP of 20 with SL 30 and straddle the same 60. 281 possible trades. Anything from 60-83 pips up is a bad trade stopped out. Anything from 84+ pips is a good trade. Out of 281 trades, 52 bad trades and 229 good trades. So gains would be 4580, losses would be 1560. Total net profit would be 3020 pips. Last scenerio, TP of 90, SL 30, straddle still 60 pips. Need a move of 154 to take profit. Anything from 60-153 is a bad trade. 154+ is a good trade. 83 good trades and 198 bad trades. Gains = 7470. Losses = 5940. Total profit = 1530. So what happened? Why did net profits go down in the last scenerio? We crossed the equilibrium point for that SL level. We started to become less efficient. This is what we need to find. We have the SL level since we set it ourselves. We have the data to show us the probabilities of our TP being hit. All we need to do is input the years of input into excel and see how many days would have been losing trades. I doubt the percentages will fluctuate that much over the years to drastically affect our profits so long as we use many years worth of data. This is all this system ever needs to be to be a successful money maker. One straddle, one TP level, and one SL level. The big problem right now is determining the SL level. Looking at the years of data in excel does not show the swings throughout a day. Unfortunately our results are drastically affected by our SL. We want a SL to allow the winners to stay winners but the big losses prevented. Is 50 SL enough for a daily chart? Maybe only 40 or do we need 70? A system can still be made profitable with a SL of 100 and a lesser TP. What will lead to someone losing money with the system is them forcing too much out of the system. This system can be automated easily, but it may not produce bank breaking numbers. (That's yet to be determined)You have to be willing to accept only a certain amount of profit. The second you stretch more out of it is the second you take it into an inefficient zone. It will correct you automatically though. Thats the beauty of equilibriums. What do you all think? Agree/disagree? If you agree I think the goal right now would be to find the smallest SL that doesn't take away our winning trades. The lower the better! Matt

--- 帖子 #394 ---
By the way, another thought that has been running through my head is spreading this system over several currencies. I don't think that would be wise though. What should be done is to explore other currencies success rates. Say the efficiency of the system on GBP/USD is 2:1 where for every dollar you lose you profit 2. If on EUR/GBP the efficiency is 1.5:1 why would you ever trade the system there? You would always want to trade the 2:1 system. Notice I said dollars and not pips since pips vary in value across currencies. The dollar profit margins would have to be calculated after the research is done and not simply by how many pips would have been won/lost. Economics is so useful! Matt

Howdy llambert, GFT doesn't show what day of the week a date is. So I had to manually look on my computer calender. Our success rates depend on our TP levels. I only gave examples in my previous post to show that we shouldn't be looking for multiple TP levels. There is an efficient point out there which I haven't found yet. So I can't say exactly what the success rates where considering I haven't given a TP level yet. For sake of argument we'll assume I entered trades on up days with a 60 pip straddle and was only looking for a 5 pip profit. (This kept the losing days to a minimum so I could quickly see what days of the week they were.) I may have counted wrong in my first post, but I only see 26 bad trades now. Meaning the up movement hit 60-68 which would not have allowed me to exit with a 5 pip profit. Here is the breakdown of what days of the week those losing days were. Sunday - 8 Monday - 5 Tuesday - 3 Wednesday - 5 Thursday - 5 Friday - 0 I will now note that my data is formed from candles that open at 5 PM Pacific Time. I'm in Arizona. I think this means my candles form at 00:00 GMT. Correct? Unfortunately the data set is small. Except for Friday and Sunday trades I think the numbers are pretty evenly averaged out. Meaning, it would not be worth while to count out certain days over others since they play relatively the same. I believe if a larger data set it used then friday and sunday will average out the same as well. The only way to play each day differently is to look at the probabilities from those days discreetly. For example, see how many Tuesdays had the greater movement up. How far up did it move up from the open? How far did it move down from the open? How does this compare to the typical Wednesday movement? There are more questions to break it down, but I'm not going to complicate things right now. I don't have the capabilities to look at any weekday specifically so I can not create a system for different days. You seem to be able to and I see nothing wrong in doing so. You'd essentially be creating 5 different variations of the same system. Something we should consider though is trader psychology. In the quick data I have looked at there was not one single up day that stalled at 61 pips up. It went from 5 days stalling at 60+ then only a few days at 62+, 63+ and then several at 65+. I think I can safely say this is because of traders using even numbers to make their trades. So I think we should alter our straddle accordingly to our TP. We could have saved 5 trades from stalling on us if we had simply entered at 1 pip more, or 61+ from open. Oddly enough, there was only one day that stalled at 70+ and then no days at 71+ or 72+. Then there is one day at 73+ and several days at 75+. We should find a level that has few days of stalling on it, but also compliments our TP such that we're allowing enough opportunities to reach our TP. We can't put a straddle of 100 and expect to TP of 80 many times. Right now I think a 61 pip straddle could be best since it will filter out being on the wrong side of the candle much of the time and still allows a candle to move many pips on an average day. If we have a 30 TP it is not unreasonable to expect it to get hit frequently; even a 40 may not be unheard of. I'm starting to wonder if we should use only 2006 data to come up with our probabilities though. Did GBP/USD trade in 2004 like it trades now?

--- 帖子 #409 ---
62a94 - I do not have an EA capable platform so I am doing manual backtesting through excel. Therefore I can't tell you if the SL would have been hit before becoming a winning trade. My results are based on if the up move would have eventually allowed to exit with the TP. If it didn't then I made the trade an automatic worst case scenerio with a total SL hit. I think the results will still hold for the following reason. There would have been trades that I counted as being stopped out but, if allowed to continue trading into the next days candle, would have closed in profit. So I believe the results would have averaged out in the end anyways. My point of post 394 however was to debate the use of the multiple TP levels. I think it is inefficient. I was using the scenerios to give examples of how we can find the true efficient level of profit maximization. The SL plays a huge part in this and we should focus on that right now. I think the 61 pip straddle is a good point. Now we need to find a SL that allows our plays to move and close in profits while still protecting us from ultimate system failure. Would a simple trailing stop work best? I base this on the idea that a price will only retrace a certain amount. Can we expect a price to rise 60 then retrace 70 before running 100 pips to close 40 above the intial 60 rise? That would be an EXTREME day of trading. The system isn't looking for extreme cases though. We're looking for the typical trade days to maximize profits through consistency. So maybe a 70 SL is too large and excessive. A 10 SL is too close, 70 too far, maybe 40? We should probably look into making our SL something like 41 as well to make it an awkward number unlikely to get stopped out on. Matt

ok, you went about it differently than me I suppose. I liked Mircardo's 50 straddle, so I went backtesting. At first, just September -15m to get accurate s/l data. I noticed far too often it hit his 50 then reversed. I kept increasing it until I came to the solution of 60. What I have is a spreadsheet for each day. Beside the date I put levels of 5, 10, 15, 20, 25 up to 70. If after the 60 straddle hit it went up say 40 pips, I subtraced my 5 spread and said that day produced 35 pips. I then put the number in each column (ie 5, 10, 15, 20, 25, 30, 35) If after it went up 40, it reversed and fell drastically to hit the s/l, I put the s/l (in my case -$40) in the other columns up to the 70 columns. If the trade stalled and the day closed (either positive or negative) I closed the trade at whatever the open of the new day was and the result was put in the other columns up to the 70 column. So after September I decided to go back from March to now. A friend of mine was reviewing the data with me. He suggested looking at the days of week, and even if one Thursday failed, the chances of the next Thursday failing. He gave me the ideas, I did the work.. LOL At first I did percentages based on whether the trade was positive or negative (regardless of whether it hit the number for that column - meaning if for column 35 pip, the trade closed at end of day with only +12, I counted it as a winner). Then we broke it down to whether the actual pp was met for a percentage. Finally, we broke each set of data out for the days of the week. I had Monday - Friday broken out into sections. I looked at these percentages and it was amazing. Wednesday alone from 3/8/06 to today for 5 pips up to 70 would all be a net negative number. So why trade Wednesdays? I choose to ignore Wednesday. Monday was positve across the board, but barely, like less than 100 pips since March, so it too was useless to me. As far as your other questions. Yes, your 5 pm is my 8 pm which is start of new day. I also did as you regarding straddle. I found 87 straddle weeded out a ton of problem days for 15 pips profit. You had to wait sometimes 3 days to 6 days to get in. I wanted something to trade more on. Also the day I tried it, it failed on 3 lots YIKES so I thought crap that didn't work. Finally, finally, you are right about us using 2006 data. My friend on the percentage thing is worried because we don't have Nov-Feb data. He wants to use the Month idea too.

--- 帖子 #427 ---
Hi permanentjaun, I really enjoyed your posts, so I'd like to share some ideas I found out after about 3 years of research and backtesting of different systems. I think efficiency is not the main goal of a system. In my oppinion consistency is the main goal and in fact I think consistency is the holly grail. If your system makes pips very consistently, it doesn't matter how many pips, you can leverage and compound that into milions of $$$$ in a couple of years. For me it's very easy to find out what are the optimal parameters for your straddle system. I can find optimal Timing, optimal SL, optimal TP using my homegrown optimization algorithms. But what happens is that we curve fit your system to the history, which I can guarantee it will not repeat in the future in the same way. However by using multiple lots with different SL and TP, it will not make most pips (wont be most efficient), but it will be more STABLE . So it will be less curve fitted to the past and will have more potential to be more consistent in the future. Could you please share your excel backtested results with us? Robert {link removed, see rule 3}

--- 帖子 #430 ---
I'm going to have to disagree with you. If you want consistency then we would look for a system that only gets 1 or 2 pips a day. Yes we could use the power of compounding to make those 1 or 2 pips worth a lot of money. The problem is even 1 or 2 pips isn't 100% guaranteed. Say the system is a remarkable 98% successful for 1 pip. The 2% of the losing times our order is stopped out for a 30 pip loss. So for every 100 trades we have 98+ gain with 60 loss. Total profit is only 38 pips. Now alter the system to a 2 TP and 30 SL. The system is only 95% accurate now. (Still a very high success rate) Out of 100 trades we would have 180+ gain and still 60 loss. Net profit is 120 pips. The first scenerio is more consistent than the second, but the second is more efficient. By keeping the SL the same and doubling our TP we have effectively increased our expected profits by 300%. This is why I don't think using multiple TP levels really helps us. There is a point which correlates with the SL we select that will give us a maximum expected payout. To further the above scenerios I will show you the equilibrium point for similar situations. Say we have a SL of 30. We have TP levels of 10,20,30,40,50,60,70,80, and 90. For each TP level we have varying success rates as follows. 10 TP is 90%, 20 TP is 80%, 30 TP is 70%, 40 TP is 60%, 50 TP is 50%, 60 TP is 40%, 70 TP is 30%, 80 TP is 20%, and 90 TP is 10%. The expected payouts out of 100 trades would be: 10 TP = 900 pips gain - 300 loss = +600 pips 20 TP = 1600 pips gain - 600 loss = +1000 pips 30 TP = 2100 pips gain - 900 loss = +1200 pips 40 TP = 2400 pips gain - 1200 loss = +1200 pips 50 TP = 2500 pips gain - 1500 loss = +1000 pips 60 TP = 2400 pips gain - 1800 loss = +600 pips 70 TP = 2100 pips gain - 2100 loss = 0 pips 80 TP = 1600 pips gain - 2400 loss = -600 pips 90 TP = 900 pips gain - 2700 loss = -1800 pips It's simple economics. So the optimal TP level for a 30 SL given the success rates given is either 30 or 40. Making a quick calculation shows 35 TP, given an assumed 65% success rate gives us +1225 pips. Efficiency means just as much about consistency as it does maximizing profit. A 10 TP may be consistent but it sure isnt the best profit level. I'm suggesting that instead of having multiple TP levels to average it out, we look for that optimum TP level. That way we aren't losing pips when we look for only 5 TP or the more rare 80 TP. There is an equilibrium point that will maximize profits somewhere and it's not at multiple points. We may not find the true equilibrium point, but we can come close such that people will have similar success. Such as if they used a 30 or 40 TP as illustrated above. Expected payouts would still be very close. The first step we need is to find out a small enough SL that won't turn winners into losers, then we go from there. I'm hoping it's no more than 40. Unfortunately I don't have any conclusive data to show you from my excel backtesting more than what I've already shared. I think a 61 straddle will work well with filtering out bad trades. I'm looking for opinions on a SL and then I can find the optimum TP for a 61 straddle by coming up with success rates for different TP levels from historical data. How do you all think I should go about looking at the data. Only use 1 years worth of data or all of it? There are several periods of time when gbp/usd traded very differently than it does now. Take a look at March 2002 to June 2002. A year before that involved many large pip days, but overall movement over several months stayed relatively flat. If we're to build the success rates for this system I think we should either use only 1 years worth of data or at least 10 years. If we look at 2-3 years then odd trading years will affect the results dramatically. By using 10 years or more we can expect that GBP/USD would have traded similar to it does now, or will in the future, and therefore the SL, TP, and success rates we find will be able to stand the test of time. Matt

So not including these days would affect the results I've posted for the better. Also, going back to the 4th July, it interested me to note that the 5th &amp; 6th July were also losing trades (the 3rd was a winning trade). Perhaps there is something to be said for not trading this method around major holidays as the volume is light and therefore the movement is erratic. 0.0012 &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;/TD&gt;&lt;TD style="BORDER-RIGHT: #ece9d8; PADDING-RIGHT: 0in; BORDER-TOP: #ece9d8; PADDING-LEFT: 0in; PADDING-BOTTOM: 0in; BORDER-LEFT: #ece9d8; PADDING-TOP: 0in; BORDER-BOTTOM: #ece9d8; HEIGHT: 12.75pt; BACKGROUND-COLOR: transparent" u1:num="2.5299999999999878E-2"&gt; 0.0253 &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;/TD&gt;&lt;/TR&gt;&lt;/TBODY&gt;&lt;/TABLE&gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; Those counter trend numbers strike me as relatively small if you ask me. Lets use a 61 straddle with a 100 SL. Where should our TP be? The following scenerios are on up weeks. &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; Let's try a 150 TP. We need 215 pip movement. This happened 19 times for a gain of 2850. Assuming worst case scenerio we would have lost 11 times for a loss of 1100. In those same candles it would have triggered 12 trades on the counter side for a loss of 1200. So only 550 pip profit. Very inefficient.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; Let's try a 50 TP. So 61 straddle requires a 54+61 = 115 pip move. On the UP weeks we would have hit that target EVERY SINGLE TIME. The gain would be 1500. BUT, there would have been trades triggered on the opposite side since our trigger is small. There would have been 12 trades triggered where 3 would have hit our TP and 9 losing. So 1500+150-900. 750 pip profit. Better than the first scenerio. You're averaging about 125 pips a month at that rate since these stats are only half a year or so. (The other half of the year are down weeks)&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; I have a theory that a better equilibrium point will be where some of the trades in the correct direction do not close for profit. By allowing one or two of those to not close in profit we may gain by allowing many fewer counter trend trades to happen. Meaning we will sacrifice 2 of our winning trades to prevent making 4 losing trades. Let's try a 92 straddle with 50 TP. Still a 100 SL. We need 145 pips to close in TP.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; 28 trades on the good side of the trend. 1400 pips. 2 not closing so -200. 4 trades triggered on the counter trend side. 2 hit TP and 2 do not. So total profits will be 1400+100-200-200 = 1100 pips. Averaging about 183 pips a month at that rate. Decent right?&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; Looking at down weeks using the last scenario data of 92 straddle, 50 TP, and 100 SL we get the following results. 22 trades occurring on the main trend side. 19 would close for profit and 3 a loss. 650 profit. 4 trades triggered on the down side, all lose. Net gain is 250 pips. Over all the weeks then our total pip gain is 1350 or about 112 a month. Those numbers aren’t so impressive. This means that we probably shouldn’t use the same straddle and TP for down weeks. &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; I don’t want to further this post any more since it is about to get even more confusing with numbers and scenerios. Once I change the straddle and TP for up vs down situations then it also changes the previous results. I’ll try and clean things up later. &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; I’m also going to test the possibility of a trailing stop loss. Is a 100 trailing stop loss large enough to prevent our week long trades from being stopped out? I’ve already shown that it’s possible to make nearly 200 pips a month using a simple 100 SL. If the large 100 trailing stop loss doesn’t stop out any winning trades, but saves the losers from being complete 100 pip losses to perhaps only 50-80 then it will greatly affect our profit margins. &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; I’m starting to wonder how much more one could make by using the same strategies for shorter time frames. Is it worth it? If I can find a way to have expected profits of 150-200 pips a month would it be worth it to be in front of the computer to trade the strategy on a daily or intraday timeframe? What if trading it on a daily chart only nets another 50 pips a month? Maybe if we can get an EA to successfully carry out the trades it might be. Right now I may be leaning towards the weekly chart though. 30-50 avg pips a week is enough for me. Power of compounding will make it very worth while. &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; I haven’t checked yet, but I’m hoping 100 SL on a weekly chart is enough. Considering the small counter trend shadows on the weekly charts I have to assume that price rarely rises 92 pips then reverses over 100 pips to form the shadow before rocketing 200-400 pips in the original direction to form the body. It’s not impossible mathematically, but if either side had that much control over the price then they wouldn’t allow for the 100 pip reverse. Understand? Anyways, would like to hear everyones thoughts. Where do you all stand on this? Thanks. Matt

But, would it produce more profit to trade each pair since it will produce more trades or would putting more into each play of the 90% pair work better? Thoughts anyone? Matt

--- 帖子 #443 ---
Having studied Risk Management in good depth at a graduate level, it would very much depend on the correlation Coefficient of the two systems, if it improves the RISK adjusted returns then it would be worth trading both pairs. Remember it would be worth trading it on less correlated pairs as these would more likely give u a lower correlation of teh two systems. Here is a site (see below) which provides the correlation of differnt pairs over different time horizons. I have various system, some for futures others for Spot FX. For the FX systems i intentially trade the systems over the least correlated pairs, i.e my divergence and hidden divergence system i only trade on GBP, CAD, AUD and NZD (note not the EUR and CHF, highly correlated with the GBP). The system does not work so well on USDJPY, GBPJPY and EURJPY, otherwise i might also trade it on these. http://www.dailyfx.com/story/chartin...eyword=article

--- 帖子 #444 ---
Carlos, Great post although you'll probably have to edit it out soon. Some thoughts though. If we find a system that works well with a currency, such as GBP/USD, then wouldn't we want to find currencies that actually trade very similar to it? I say this because if we can find a currency that is equally as successful on GBP/USD then we would want to use it in the hopes that when one currency hasn't triggered a trade yet, the other currency, moving in a similar but altered manner, will have triggered a trade. My thought process is that we never want more than one trade to be happening at one time. If we have two trades occuring at once we should always have the desire to have all of the funds trading in the more successful system. Why put money into a 50% successful currency when you can trade one that is 85% successful. Considering equal pip values and such, the 85% successful currency will always produce greater profit in the long run. That is why we might want to look for highly correlated pairs in the hopes that they trigger equally sucessful, but at different times so that we can always have money playing the success rates. If we have a 90% successful pair it is nice, but if it only triggers 1 trade a month for 10 pips then it's not as profitable as the 70% successful system that triggers 10 trades a month. Matt

--- 帖子 #454 ---
Hi Matt, If Merlin checks he will notice its a link from an FXCM site, i assure u i wouldn't recommend anyone to trade with them... just my view!! Great post although you'll probably have to edit it out soon. Some thoughts though. If we find a system that works well with a currency, such as GBP/USD, then wouldn't we want to find currencies that actually trade very similar to it? I say this because if we can find a currency that is equally as successful on GBP/USD then we would want to use it in the hopes that when one currency hasn't triggered a trade yet, the other currency, moving in a similar but altered manner, will have triggered a trade. uumm, i understand what your saying, but i don't think this is an ideal situation. The more diversification u can add to your trading the better, PERIOD. There are two types of risk, systematic risk and unsystematic risk. Market traders are never rewarded for systematic risk (i.e risk that can be diversified out of the portfolio by diversification of systems, markets and time frames) Please this is a very very important topic. Having institutional experience (now trying to biuld my own business) i can assure u that an employer would hammer u if u didn't respect this!! What if the system was triggered on both currecnies at the same time, this might happen more frequently than u might expect. In this situation your risk would be doubled up, even trippled! Also to cancel orders u would need to be constantly around your computer to know when one of your entry orders has been triggered. My thought process is that we never want more than one trade to be happening at one time. If we have two trades occuring at once we should always have the desire to have all of the funds trading in the more successful system. Why put money into a 50% successful currency when you can trade one that is 85% successful. Considering equal pip values and such, the 85% successful currency will always produce greater profit in the long run. U can have more than one trade open at any one time if the markets are not overly correlated, yes there is intermarket analysis where all markets are linked with one another, hence why u might never have more than 3 or 4 positions open at any one time, but it is ok to have more than one trade open. Here u also talk about just trading one system, here i also say, systematic risk. All system, even 85% accurate will go through periods of drawdown (a statistical fact), also 85% accurate systems are very hard to find, my systems are based around Risk to Reward rather than % accurate That is why we might want to look for highly correlated pairs in the hopes that they trigger equally sucessful, but at different times so that we can always have money playing the success rates. If we have a 90% successful pair it is nice, but if it only triggers 1 trade a month for 10 pips then it's not as profitable as the 70% successful system that triggers 10 trades a month. Matt[/quote] Why not find uncorrelated pairs which trigger at diff times, catch different moves and therefore give u a smoother equity curve while having a high success rate. The best systems (as a rule of thumb) work on different timeframes and markets, it is a good test of the validity of a system. Of course small adjustments need to be made for the different market behaviours, but they should be done in an intelligent manner, with logical reasoning, rather than curve fitting. However; i do have a fantastic system which only really works on one currecny (GBPUSD) and only on the 15 min chart. I recommend two books: 1) Designing testing and Optimization of trading Systems, Robert Pardo, Wiley Traders Advantage. 2) This book is on the practical application of Excel spread sheet modeling, includes many advanced risk management tools. Will be heavy reading if your new to this stuff. Financial Modeling, Benningo, MIT Press Good luck, i'm away till Tuesday on a stag weekend in Prague!!

--- 帖子 #457 ---
Yes. I've had a good time over the last couple of weeks trading a kind of modified Kamanda system. You can find his posts earlier in this thread. I have been placing straddle trades at 5 PM EST on the GBPUSD daily open. For long trades I require a travel of 54 pips. For short trades I now use 40. Stops were at the beginning 50 for longs and 35 for shorts. I have changed to 54 for longs and 40 for shorts. I use two lots per trade. One is set for a TP of 25 and the other for 50. Usually by around 10 AM EST I close out the second trade if not already stopped by SL or TP. I call the small trade T1 and the larger trade T2 on the enclosed spreadsheet. Started on Nov 7 and ended on Nov22. I didn't trade Friday because I still feel on Holiday! So far I like this method and it hasn't required a lot of nervous screen time. I call it Karamba just for my own amusement. Enjoy. (282 pips so far).

--- 帖子 #459 ---
Hello all, I just had a quick revelation for finding equilibriums. I've been looking at things quite awkwardly when it's all pretty simple actually. We can't force the market to do anything. So why should we force our TP's and triggers? We should look at the data to see where the most pips are available. It is so easy. http://img19.imageshack.us/img19/5532/graph1pn0.png I've been looking at charts like this all day for the past couple of days. This is a chart from a weekly chart. It is for the down weeks in the last 52 weeks. The x-axis shows the frequency of the pip movements. The y-axis shows just how many pips the price moved. In this case it is for the down weeks, so the y-axis numbers are how many pips down from the open the price moved. I've been trying to find a way to determine trigger points and TP levels. My initial reaction was to look at the curve of the overall slope and find where it changes dramatically showing points where pip movements became more radical. It's not so apparent on this chart since it's a very small data set. If you saw a chart with 1000 candles of data then you'd easily see what I'm talking about. It begins to curve up exponentially as you approach the y-axis from the right. Anyways, it was actually looking at small data sets like that which made the simple easy to see. All we need to do is find the bar on the above chart that has the most area. For example, bar 8 would be (8)(.0253), the red lines, and bar 22 would be (22)(.0111), the yellow lines. Therefore the areas would be .2024 and .2442 respectively. Logic would then kick in and tell us more pips are possible if we play a system that only plays for the 111 pip, .0111, movement on a down move. On the above chart the point with maximum possible pips would be playing a system that exits after -181 pips movement from open. This is because it would have happened 17 out of the 22 times allowing for a system to play with 3077 possible pips to maximize profit in a little less than half a year. From there we just have to find the efficient point that maximizes profit with a given SL. I just had to get this down just so I don't have a brain fart and lose it even though it's such a simple concept. Instead of stabbing in the dark with numbers we at least have a starting point. We know that the most possible pips in a down movement are when we look to be out of the trade when it has moved -181 pips from open. I'm slowly trying to fill in the variables. I have had a thought come to mind recently though. Perhaps this system isn't meant for an EA. I mean it could be, but to remain efficient maybe it shouldn't. Once I get the process down to finding the efficient points quickly it might be best to only use a years worth of data and redo the calculations once a week or daily depending on if you're playing a weekly or daily chart. So I would add this weeks data over the weekend to the calculations and take away the week that was one year ago. Since price movement evolves over time the system calculations should be able to do so as well. Anyways, just wanted to get that out. I'll try to determine the efficient trigger point given a 100 SL and that we must exit the trade once it has moved -181 from open. Matt

--- 帖子 #461 ---
Some quick looks show that for the data from these 22 down weeks, the optimum point for profit maximization would be an 81 pip straddle with 96 TP + 4 pip spread. This is with a given 100 SL. The SL determines the profits levels entirely. If we assumed to use the same straddle to the upside of 81 pips then there would have been 27 trades triggered in the 22 weeks since we are allowed 2 possible trades per candle; one long and one short. 17 of those trades would have ended in profit. 17 X 96 = 1632. 1632 - 1000 loss = 632 pips profit. 632/6 = 105 pips a month for down trades. I'm not sure how I should feel about that. Are those pips more guaranteed than any other system? 17 out of 27 trades is 63% correct. Would power of compounding make those 105 pips a month worth a lot in a year or two such that we're not bored with making only 105 pips? This is from a simple weekly system on down trades. I'm wondering what the results will be like when I look at a daily chart using a years worth of data. Will we be able to pull profits more consistently or frequently then that to produce 150 pips or more a month? I don't know about you, but I'm getting excited. I think a system such as this has more potential to survive the long run than most other systems based around emotion and chart reading. If we replace old data with new data to come up with new trigger and TP levels each week/day then it should keep us winning on the average for the current time no matter what type of trading is occuring. Anyone disagree with me or think I'm finding my efficient trigger and TP points incorrectly? Matt
