BORDER-LEFT: #ece9d8; BORDER-BOTTOM: #ece9d8; BACKGROUND-COLOR: transparent" align=right x:num="1.0900000000000132E-2" x:fmla="=C23-E23"&gt; 0.0109 &lt;/TD&gt;&lt;TD style="BORDER-RIGHT: #ece9d8; BORDER-TOP: #ece9d8; BORDER-LEFT: #ece9d8; BORDER-BOTTOM: #ece9d8; BACKGROUND-COLOR: transparent" align=right x:num="1.1099999999999888E-2" x:fmla="=E23-D23"&gt; 0.0111 &lt;/TD&gt;&lt;TD style="BORDER-RIGHT: #ece9d8; BORDER-TOP: #ece9d8; BORDER-LEFT: #ece9d8; BORDER-BOTTOM: #ece9d8; BACKGROUND-COLOR: transparent" align=right x:num="-1.9999999999975593E-4" x:fmla="=G23-H23"&gt; -0.0002 &lt;/TD&gt;&lt;TD style="BORDER-RIGHT: #ece9d8; BORDER-TOP: #ece9d8; BORDER-LEFT: #ece9d8; BORDER-BOTTOM: #ece9d8; BACKGROUND-COLOR: transparent" align=right x:num="0.24419999999999753" x:fmla="=A23*H23"&gt; 0.2442 &lt;/TD&gt;&lt;/TR&gt;&lt;/TBODY&gt;&lt;/TABLE&gt; First five columns are self explanatory. They include the date and OHLC. The next columns I had to figure out what we are concerned with in this system. We only care about maximums. So I originally took the data from all 52 weeks and did the following. Column "high - open" calculates the absolute up move from open. Column "open - low" calculates the absolute down move from open. Then I made a calculation to simply subtract the "high - open" column minus the "open - low" column. This gives us the values for the "up vs. down" column. In this case they're all negative because these are what I labeled as the down weeks. The movement to the downside was greater then that of the move to the upside. The up weeks are on another spread sheet. The last column, "frequency", is really the area of the bars on the graph I showed you. You need to sort the "open-low" column in descending order then label each row 1-22. The calculation for the frequency column would then be (1-22) X (open-low). This way the extreme move of .0471 multiplies by the number 1 since it only happened once out of the 22 weeks. The 111 pip move down would be multiplied by 22 since each down week would have moved at least 111 pips down. The maximum point in our "frequency" column is our efficient level that we can expect a price to move down on down weeks. This occurs when frequency = .3136 or when we expect a down week to move 196 pips down. Wow, sorry I messed up in my previous posts. Must be getting late for me to miss that. I'll wrap up this post and edit my previous posts. Just want to get my simple spreadsheets out there so you can all see what I'm doing. Matt

--- 帖子 #463 ---
Ok a quick look again shows that if we expect a down week to move -196 pips from open then we should set our trigger around -122 or so. We can then take a profit of 66 and get 622 pips profit for the 6 months. But, you scream, "622 is less than 632 which was the expected profit when using -181 as our exit point." This is true. I think these calculations prove my point further that we should always be replacing the oldest data with the newest to keep up with current movement behaviors. This system is about averaging because we're basing everything on typical ranges and expectencies. In reality, the 196 pip movement is still the more profitable because all I need to do is say we should institute a 117 pip straddle with 79 TP. That would have eliminated all the counter trend moves and even 1 of the major trend moves that would have ended in a SL. In this case the profits would have been 16 X 79 = 1264 - 500 pip loss = 764 net profit. But this would involve us eliminating one of the 100 SL trades by placing our trigger 1 pip above the maximum counter trend value in hindsight to reduce our losses greatly. So the 196 expected move is still the profitable expected behavior. Perhaps we should have instituted the 117 trigger and 79 immediately after that one example week failed? Sorry, but I don't know how else to explain it without making things confusing. Anyways, digest that and let me know what you think. Thanks. Matt

BORDER-LEFT: #ece9d8; BORDER-BOTTOM: #ece9d8; BACKGROUND-COLOR: transparent" align=right x:num="0.40800000000000169" x:fmla="=A31*G31"&gt; 0.408 &lt;/TD&gt;&lt;/TR&gt;&lt;/TBODY&gt;&lt;/TABLE&gt; A quick look shows that for this sheet we should expect up moves of 211 pips and have a system based around it. As you can see, there are many "frequency" values similar to our efficient point of .422. I imagine that this is only because I am using very little data. If we used more data, such as many years worth, then there would be a certain point that is clearly the most efficient point. Anyways, I quickly found that somewhere around a 91 trigger with 116 TP is the most efficient. This would have produced 34 trades out of the 30 weeks. 20 would have ended in profit with 14 getting stopped out in our worst case scenerios. So 20 X 116 = 2320 - 1400 = 920 net pips for these 30 weeks. That's about 145 pips a month. Again, using a trailing 100 SL might help us with our profit margins tremendously. Or just using a 75 pip SL would work better. Not sure. Here's the problem. Our expected profits from this and previous posts are now thrown out the window. What can we expect if we use a 91 straddle with 116 TP on up moves and 122 straddle with 70 TP on down moves? In my previous down week calculations a lot of losing trades were thrown out because the straddle was too high. I imagine many may be thrown back in now. Let's take a look Out of the 52 weeks here is how things broke down. It was a delicate balance I'd say. Because when you combine the two systems of a 122 trigger and a 91 trigger, on the 91 trigger the opposing side, long entries, ends up better since fewer trades hit the -122 mark, on the short side, to create losing trades. On the other side, a 91 trigger hits more trades for the down week data and creates more losses. Anyways, on UP weeks we would have made profit the 20 times for 2360 profit. Then lost the 10 trades triggered. With the short side trigger -122 only 2 trades would have been triggered. Since the TP level is different for short trades too this means one would have ended in profit and one stopped out. Total profit for 30 weeks of up weeks is 1290. On down weeks we would have made our 620 profit, but the lower trigger on the up side of only 91 would have triggered 4 bad trades. Thus total profit out of 22 down weeks is only 220. 220+1290 = 1510 pips for the year or 125 pips per month. Again, not sure if I should be happy with that number or not. How will compounding play out with those pips as well as depositing more money into my account since I can expect to be in profit at the end of 52 weeks. I don't think I'd be throwing money away by doing so to increase my bank roll and available lots to intelligently place into a trade. Maybe I'll have to find a way to look at the up and down weeks at once so that triggers for up and down can be found at the same time to find a more happy equilibrium point. Sorry to post all this to make you all read it. Hope I'm not talking to myself though. All advice welcome! Matt

--- 帖子 #465 ---
I guess I can't fall asleep when I've got stuff like this on my mind. I've already solved the problem of combining the two systems. Everything keeps getting simpler and simpler the more I think about it. What was the point of me splitting the data into UP versus down weeks? What do we care if its an up or a down week just so long as we get our profits? We don't, or at least shouldn't. So essentially you can throw away the "up vs down" column. It's useless now. All we're concerned with is the frequency, high-open, and open - low columns. You do need to have seperate sheets when you calculate frequency however. Apparently my initial observations were correct as far as what levels the frequencies come up with. For up moves we should still expect to close our trades after +211 pips from open. Because the years worth of data is used then we should expect different trigger points though. For down weeks the data was a little bit different. Again, I think this is because I'm only using 52 sets of data. So it shows maximum profit potential at closing trades after -161 pips. But I believe this to be an outlier in the data set and that -196 is still the best since it was the second highest frequency value in the set and appeared more normal in comparison. For up movement the new trigger and TP with a 4 pip spread would be an 81 straddle with 126 TP which is 81+126+4 = 211 total pip movement. For down movement we would set a trigger of 96 pips and TP after 96. So 96 + 96 + 4 = 196, our expected down movement. Do 211 or 196 seem unreasonable movements to expect? I'd say they'll happen pretty often, but not always. MONEY MANAGEMENT IS KEY. Those triggers aren't exact. I simply took the levels of 211 and 196 for the respective sides, then subtracted 100 as my TP+spread to find the trigger. Then I just worked out how much profit I would have made considering the successful trades minus the losing trades. As I decreased my TP on each I made the system more successful since the trigger could then be higher and allow less losing trades triggered, but I decreased my marginal profit on the winning trades. As I increased my TP I allowed for more losing trades, but increased my marginal profit on winning trades. I just found the balance somewhere in between that made the most profit. Again, I only went up and down by 10 pips to make quick judgements, so there are probably more precise numbers that will work better with more profit margins. I imagine the numbers will be so close it doesn't affect results too much though. So how much would the system have produced? It's better than I thought. On the up movements, +81 trigger with 126 TP and 4 pip spread for 211 total movement, would have made 1020 net pips. For down movements, -96 trigger with 96 TP and 4 pip spread for 196 total down movement, would have made 732 pips. Total pips out of the 52 weeks = 1752 or about 146 pips each month. Not bad huh? Better than the 125 pips in the previous month. I essentially just improved the efficiency of the system by 17% just by making my calculations easier. KEEP IT SIMPLE STUPID. Argh. I'll make another advocacy for the evolving system. Replace the oldest data set with the newest data set. There are different triggers and TP's because this year probably included more up weeks than down weeks. (It did as noted by my previous spreadsheets showing 30 up weeks vs. 22 down weeks.) So in the next year when there are more down weeks than up weeks the system will evolve to stay in a happy equilibrium. If you don't keep it updated it will correct your bank account for you! Now that I have found the calculations easily I think it could be a pretty useful system to run while you work full time. 10 minutes of figuring out profit maximizing points on a saturday while the market is off, and you're making 146 pips a month. Sounds pretty good right? And that's assuming worst case scenerios of our 100 SL getting hit on every trade that didn't complete itself that week. What about trades that win in the next weeks candle? Or what if we instituted a 100 trailing stop loss to cut down on our losses? It would greatly affect our results. More greatly affecting the results would be reducing the SL to 75 or so. I'm afraid of cutting into our winners though. Hope you all got something out of this. I think I have. Feel free to correct my thought process please. No one ever learned anything by being told they were always doing things right. TIA. Matt

--- 帖子 #485 ---
I meant when we only look at the weekly candles in backtesting, we can miss instances where on the 1 hour or daily charts the trade was triggered (say at a +100 move), then retraced to stop out at 100, then once again shot back up to hit what we set for take profit. On the weekly charts those activities can sometimes be hidden and we would count a win, when in fact we would see on the daily or hourly charts that it was a loss. I was not using any kind of trailing stop in this instance. At this point I think even to test a weekly strategy we have to use at least the daily charts to get more accurate data.

--- 帖子 #500 ---
buy 1.9527 sell stop-loss 1.9497 (25s/l + 5 spread = 30 total) sell limit 1.9545 (23 - 5 spread = 18 net) If you wanted 23 net profit, limit would be 1.9550. I wouldn't do that with the s/l though. sell 1.9478 buy stop-loss 1.9508 (in trade system 1.9508 is the ask price. When the ask is this, the bid is 1.9503, which is 25s/l) buy limit 1.9460 (same thing) You need to make an excel spreadsheet and put formulas in. It is a whole lot easier just plugging in some numbers and let excel calculate the numbers to use than doing it in your head. I got a headache giving you the example.

Well I wrote a program that takes the 15 m date since 1999, breaks it down by day and year and allows for different straddle on a daily basis. Trust me, nothing works consistently. The only way to win is to find the best straddle that prevents the most consecutive losing days in a row and double up when you lose, and hope it isn't 2002, 2003, and 2004. --- 帖子 #505 ---
Also, I don't understand what you are talking about really. If I use a 70 straddle using bid price of 1.9000, the straddle is 1.9075(ask) and 1.8930 (BID) that is raw data. If I want a 30 pip profit, on long side I sell at 1.9105(BID) or 1.9110 ask. The ask price is 35 pips - 5 pip spread gives 30. All I care about is whether the bid price hits 1.9105, then it is a winner. Same with s/l.

--- 帖子 #506 ---
Because changing the SL affects the system. Using a 70 straddle takes away a lot of potential plays. Perhaps it only reaches 70 pips to the upside 20% of the time. What TP do you set? Well a 10 pip TP will be hit 60% of the time, 20 TP 40% of the time, 30 TP 20% of the time. What should your TP then be? It depends on if you're using a 20, 30, or 40 SL. As you increase the TP, your SL gets hit more often since less and less trades end successfully. It's the idea that you can win 99 times out of 100 and make 5 pips per trade for a net gain of 495 pips. There's going to be that one losing trade, and the system is bad if on that trade you lose 500 pips. -5 pips for the 100 trades. The SL affects the risk/reward potential and therefore the equilibrium point shifts around it. It has to do with the marginal profits of increasing your TP. How much marginal profit does a 20 SL or 50 SL give when you want to look for 5 more pips in TP? If 5 more trades lose because of the higher TP is that another 100 pips in the loss category or 250? It's a big deal determining the system around the SL.

--- 帖子 #507 ---
yes you are exactly right. That is why you need to have a separate program to play with the s/l. In my program, you can change the s/l for any given day of week (or everyday) and re-process the data. It looks at each consecutive 15 m candle to determine if the s/l is hit. If it is, it records the highest pip value to that point (minus the spread). The 5 pip spread is then added to the s/l. So if I were using 70 straddle, with a 30 tp and 30 s/l, then 25 is recorded as profit OR 35 is recorded as s/l depending on what I want. The thing is that I believe I have found the perfect straddle on gbp/usd, and most days of the week the straddle works, but not on other days. Changing the other days works well. However, using the same criteria for 2005 does not produce positive results. BUT maybe it isn't meant to all be positive, but a higher percentage of wins, so that when you lose, you double up to negate the losses. I can tell you the straddle I am using didn't start working on its own (without doubling up) until April 2006, but has since worked and continues to work. At what point does it stop though? That is the question.

--- 帖子 #508 ---
Partly why I believe that this system works best by having a revolving data set. Meaning the oldest data should be replaced by the newest. That was it evolves over time along with the trading pattern of the currency. Another way it will work is to use data spanning years and years such that all trading patterns are covered. I used the methods in my previous posts to look at all the data on a weekly chart back to 1987. Yes, 1987. For up weeks I originally found that we should be exiting our trades after 211 pips. That was using only 52 weeks of data. It wasn't too far from the 19 year data equilibrium. Out of 19 years of weekly data, looking to exit after 188 pips up is the most efficient point. Like I said, it's not always an exact science. As you can see 186-189 seems to be a sweet spot to take profits at. 211 is near the top as well, so we wouldn't have been too bad using just this years data. Don't be alarmed that only one of those dates is 2006. Those are only the dates that those weeks stopped at meaning there are probably plenty of recent dates hitting 186+ pips in an upmove. We know this to be true. Perhaps this was still the correct way to find the efficient level at which we close our trades. llambert3 - I'm going to need your help finding a correct SL level. Again, it's going to be a balance to figure that out. If we get 100 pips profit from the successful trades, what happens with a 100 SL? Does it prevent 2 trades from becoming successful? What if we reduce the SL to only 70. Does it then prevent 5 trades from being successful? It still might be better to do so though if in all the losing trades it saves us more than 500 pips from being lost. Or cutting off 17 of the losing trades earlier than normal. Get what I mean? This is, again, why basing this type of system around the SL is so important. Matt

--- 帖子 #510 ---
I think if we try to analyze the same data from intraday charts then new ways of formulating things are required. Using the same methods for the intra day charts doesn't work. According to the same methods, the most pips are available for up trades if we exit our trade after it has moved 12 pips. The reason is because most of the data on a 2 hour chart is full of small candles during periods of inactivity. This strategy really isn't a break out strategy. It's an average strategy. Hehe, I mean that in a good way. The average 2 hour candle isn't very large. So if you want to play the average 2 hour candle you're only looking for small profits since the large candles don't happen on average. This gets me thinking more about the strategy. It brings me back to my question from a few days ago, "When do we know the system is successful? If we can average 100 pips a month? 150? 200?" Playing the average candle isn't going to give us 500 pip months or weeks. It's not going to usually give us -500 pip months months or weeks. What are we looking for in terms of profit? You can't push this type of system past it's limits. It will correct itself in the long run. Beauty of equilibriums. Matt

For instance I can write a program that given a trigger, tells the greatest stop loss after the trigger, but before the target. I can use your suggestion of 188 pips for weekly, and if that is hit, what the highest s/l would've been PRIOR to the 188 being hit. The trades that don't hit the 188 target within a week could possibly be excluded from the calculations since we are only interested in the s/l point before the 188 target is hit, and only if it is hit. In other words if we buy, but the trade goes down 200 pips, then reverses and eventually hits the 188 target, then 200 would be the highest s/l needed so far. Does that make sense or am I missing something? That would get us a start anyway. We may find it drop 300 or 400 pips before reversing. --- 帖子 #513 ---
I think that's the catch 22. I can't tell you a trigger until you tell me a SL. The numbers I just gave you, the 188, is the point at which we EXIT the trade. Meaning it was the most efficient number out of all the data in the up weeks where it was hit the most and was also a number to give us a high pip count. For example, 200 could have been hit 100 times for 20000 pips, but 180 was hit 200 times to give us 36000 pips to play with. Get what I'm saying? We want to know the best point to play with the most pips such that it's easiest to get our pips out of the move. So this means the trigger should actually be somewhere inbetween 0 and 188 pips. If the trigger is 60 pips then our TP is 128. If the trigger is 100 pips then our TP is 88. It depends on what the SL is because the lower the trigger, the more trades are triggered that won't be successful. With a higher SL, then the more trades triggered means much more hurt to our profits. How do I know when they're up weeks? I don't. I don't care. Remember my post saying to get rid of the "up vs down" column? This meant that I am analyzing all the up movements at once. So my data includes some weeks where the up move was only 10 pips. It also includes data of weeks where it went up 900 pips. What my data is showing is what type of move we can expect with pips going north from the open. Since there will be weeks where it will end negative, but there will still be significant up movement, we need to look at all data from every week at once. So when I say up week data I really mean its data from weekly charts showing the up movement we should expect. Sorry to confuse you. Let me know if I'm still not explaining it clearly. Matt

Hi FT, i just hacked into one of my indicators and added the prior day's close (yellow line). You can download the indicator here . In order to keep the code simple and clean i did not put the prior day's open, only it's close. You can easily see where the prior closes were with the Yellow line and extend the line yourself manualy for a good visual of the candle's Open/Close, or it's "Body". Also the day's high, low, and median is there. Hope this helps in your pippage. In the below image i have the indicator shifted 1 day. So the levels you see are the HLCM of yesterday. I placed two orange DASHed lines to indicate yesterday's close, and the day before yesterday. This would indicate the area of yesterday's "Body" with a bit of manual elbow grease...but it never hurts to get a bit dirty with placing some manual lines and getting involved with the chart in my book. Cheers, Thom http://accrete.com/fx-atm/indicators...levels-pix.png

Just wanted to post a further update on my modified Kamanda system. Been trading this since Nov7. I trade two units. Take profit at 25 pips on the first and 50 on the second. If the second hasn't closed by around 9 AM EST I close it whatever. Trigger is now 54 long and 40 short. SL is 50 long and 40 short. Using the 5 PM EST open (or close however you look at it). I deleted all of the cancelled trades that weren't triggered. I call it karamba just for fun.

--- 帖子 #533 ---
As you can see the pound dollar after a 200 pip run has already retraced to the 23.6 fib level and a little more then half way to the 38.2 fib level and now has began to rise away from it. The frequencey of it hitting the 38.2 is about .455% of the time. So more then likely it will stay above that level. It seems like everyone has accepted the fact that it will rise to 2.000 so there appears to be no psychological barrier there. It appears that way.

Below is some information in regards to what the pound does in comparison to the dollar in the month of December. Hope this helps. &lt;?xml:namespace prefix = o ns = "urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:office" /&gt;&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; This information came from the cable update thread post #240 on page 16.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; British pound – US Dollar (GBP/USD) The sterling appreciated against the U.S. dollar in the month of December, 14 out of the past 20 years times which is roughly 70 percent of the total sample. Like the EUR/USD, the seasonality factor was stronger in the last 10 years with the GBP/USD appreciating 8 years out of the last 10 samples. On average, the GBP/USD gained 2.37 percent during the positive months and lost only 1.15 percent during the negative months.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; GBP/USD closed on Nov. 30 1.9653. A 2.37 gain is 466 pips which would be 2.0119. A 1.15 loss would be 226 pips to finish the year 1.9327.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;?xml:namespace prefix = v ns = "urn:schemas-microsoft-com:vml" /&gt;&lt;v:shapetype id=_x0000_t75 stroked="f" filled="f" path="m@4@5l@4@11@9@11@9@5xe" o referrelative="t" o:spt="75" coordsize="21600,21600"&gt;&lt;v:stroke joinstyle="miter"&gt;&lt;/v:stroke&gt;&lt;v:formulas&gt;&lt;v:f eqn="if lineDrawn pixelLineWidth 0"&gt;&lt;/v:f&gt;&lt;v:f eqn="sum @0 1 0"&gt;&lt;/v:f&gt;&lt;v:f eqn="sum 0 0 @1"&gt;&lt;/v:f&gt;&lt;v:f eqn="prod @2 1 2"&gt;&lt;/v:f&gt;&lt;v:f eqn="prod @3 21600 pixelWidth"&gt;&lt;/v:f&gt;&lt;v:f eqn="prod @3 21600 pixelHeight"&gt;&lt;/v:f&gt;&lt;v:f eqn="sum @0 0 1"&gt;&lt;/v:f&gt;&lt;v:f eqn="prod @6 1 2"&gt;&lt;/v:f&gt;&lt;v:f eqn="prod @7 21600 pixelWidth"&gt;&lt;/v:f&gt;&lt;v:f eqn="sum @8 21600 0"&gt;&lt;/v:f&gt;&lt;v:f eqn="prod @7 21600 pixelHeight"&gt;&lt;/v:f&gt;&lt;v:f eqn="sum @10 21600 0"&gt;&lt;/v:f&gt;&lt;/v:formulas&gt;&lt;v ath o:connecttype="rect" gradientshapeok="t" o:extrusionok="f"&gt;&lt;/v ath&gt;&lt;o:lock aspectratio="t" v:ext="edit"&gt;&lt;/o:lock&gt;&lt;/v:shapetype&gt;&lt;v:shape id=_x0000_i1025 style="WIDTH: 446.25pt; HEIGHT: 232.5pt" alt="" type="#_x0000_t75"&gt;&lt;v:imagedata o:href="http://www.dailyfx.com/export/sites/dailyfx/story-images/2006/11/special_report/Pictures/Seasonality11.22.2006img2.gif" src="file:///C:/DOCUME~1/Owner/LOCALS~1/Temp/msoclip1/01/clip_image001.gif"&gt;&lt;/v:imagedata&gt;&lt;/v:shape&gt;&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; __________________ Emotions And Money Don't Mix &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt;

--- 帖子 #538 ---
Hello all, I haven't posted here in a while, but I have been thinking about this topic still. In the meantime I've been reading up on things such as grid trading, martingale, Hans method, etc.. I also haven't posted because I had the feeling my results from backtesting were pointing to a grim picture for the daily range strategy. Why am I posting though? I am coming back to this threads idea. The grid system is really what made it clear though. Grid trading doesn't use trend lines or chart formations. It simply uses hedging and price movement to stay on the right side of the trade. My broker, GFT, does not have hedging or EA capabilities though. So it was simple. All I had to do was take the "daily" out of the daily range strategy. I'm proposing that you simply place straddles from any current price on a chart. There's no need to bring time into this. I think something along the lines of a 200 pip straddle should be used such that it really reduces our risk of getting caught in a ranging market. Ranging markets are the devil. We won't get a trade every day, but perhaps the profits would be much more consistent? Therefore thats why I'm wondering if perhaps a martingale strategy of doubling up on losers could produce great profits. You just need an account large enough to be able to handle it. Slow steady profits. Or if a trade is stopped out immediately enter a position in the direction of the new trend at the point you get stopped out. Hope to profit off of that to overcome the previous losing trade. I think doubling up might be more fruitful. 80 good trades out of 100, with effective money management I could probably be able to double up several times in case I do happen to lose several times in a row; which begins to become severely unlikely. I think the difference would be this system exits the market to create a new trade and then double up on that trade. A true martingale strategy keeps adding to a losing position and doesn't exit the market until either profits are realized or the account has a margin call. (Ouch) When you exit the market and look for the new trade. It's new conditions so you're trading to find the trend again rather than bet that the same current trend will stop. When you try to predict tops/bottoms/reversals you get eaten up in trading. So say price is 1.9000. Place a buy order at 1.9200 and sell at 1.8800. I haven't figured out TP yet, but I'm thinking 40-50. So when a trade ends in success then find the new levels. With a 50 TP on the buy order we would be out of the market at 1.9250. Your next trade levels would be 1.9450 and 1.9050 for buy and short respectively. What do you all think? This works just like the daily range strategy because the market is always moving either up or down. When you think about it, the daily range strategy could have been implemented at any point in the day. Waiting for the new candle was really just to give us the new point to base our straddle off of. So why wait for a new candle? Just keep making trades as they come. I proposed 200 pips such that we're out of the daily range of trading and for price to move 200 pips it has to trend somehow. What do you all think? Matt

--- 帖子 #541 ---
Mark..... What would the stop loss be on this new grid system? You mentioned that we would place a trade in the other direction when we are stopped out, but I didn't catch what the stop loss would be. I've played with grids quite a bit with only so-so results. The reason I find the daily range methods interesting is because we have used some historical performance figures on which to base our "trigger" points. Usually on the GBPUSD, if the price moves 50 or 55 points from the opening, it will not come all the way back. I think that Vegas quotes that around 70% of the time, for that pair, that is true. So that is where we start. Somebody here experimented with 60 or 61 also and found it workable. What we need to do is find the best range for the TP in order to smooth out our equity curve. We could indeed straddle "breakouts" from anyplace on the charts, but I think for them to succeed more often than fail, they should be triggered using some historical patterns to gain any kind of edge. I have the past few weeks had remarkable success using Micardo's trigger of 50 either way from the FXDD opening price. To a lesser extent with the Kamanda method of a smaller trigger on shorts. I don't plan to trade on Thursday or Friday this week due to the NFP on Friday. Don't expect much movement on Thursday and the wrong kind of movement on Friday!

--- 帖子 #542 ---
Well the new idea would have to be worked out between each individual person. When looking for such massive movements on a chart, it probably wouldn't be wise to use a 30-40 SL unless we're looking for only 30-50 TP. A larger 100 SL may be needed. I haven't played with any numbers yet. Should the straddle be only 150? Should we only take 30-50 TP? 100? I think a 200 straddle with 100 TP is asking for too much movement. If you want 100 TP then lower the straddle, but then you risk getting stuck in a ranging market. You're right there is the flaw that it doesn't necessarily use historical data that is easy to play with. It is going to be a game of guess and check, or manually calculating the amplitude in a ranging market and the amiplitude of a trending market. But I can say the daily range strategy is also inherently flawed too. Its a price action system that relies much on time. If price gradually rises, the point to base the straddle off of moves with each time, and the overall movement is missed when no triggers are hit. It's also possible for the system to enter trades counter to the direction of the trend. I'm simply basing this theory off the idea that for price to move so much it must be trending in that direction and therefore more likely to give us pips. It's filtering out the noise just like the original daily strategy. Only problem I'm really seeing is the lack of trades made with a 200 straddle. From 7/12-9/11 it would have only made 8 trades. 6 winners and 2 losers. This was a 200 straddle, 50 TP, 100 SL. I doubled up on the trades following losers to bring the total pips to 200 for the 2 months. 100 pips a month. Not to impressive, but oh well. The point though, is that perhaps we don't need a time frame on the chart. In fact I think that may hurt us. What if the market ranges and the opens for several candles are very close together? You're stuck in the range. If you abandon time frames and using opening prices for straddle points, you can use random points which could inherently move your straddle outside of a range, or at least be able to profit from it. This just something to be discussed. Who's mark? Matt

--- 帖子 #544 ---
How do we let winners run though? When do we know they'll be winners? How long do we let them run? I don't think a system as simple as this one can answer these questions. In my line of thinking it may be evolving that way though. I'm trying to think of different ways of implementing the system. What if we could use hindsight to our advantage? How would it work? With a large 200 pip straddle it's possible. Rather than taking random entry points, what if we waited for a peak or valley to form on the chart, then base our entry point off of that high or low? Most likely, on an intraday chart, it is easy to see a peak or valley before it moves 200 pips. But then, how do we judge if a trend will continue for 700 pips and we can take advantage of it? It might require that we take out profits from playing the peak/valley observation idea, PVO method (hehe), as well as the original idea of placing a 200 pip straddle towards the direction of the current trend. If the trend doesn't reverse you'll enter another trade in the same direction. If it reverses, which it most likely will, you look for the peak/valley, PVO, to base a new 200 pip straddle. Just more thoughts to throw in the game. I'm sure this could be implemented on many different time frames with varying SL, TP, and trigger levels. Matt

The system pretty much guarantees 10 pips when looking for the 200 pip move. Does that mean we should only exit after 10 pips? If we look for 50 pips we'll say the system is 70% correct. (Not sure of that figure) Looking for 60 pips is 60%, 70 pips 50%. I'd rather take the 50 pips and always stay at 70% than introduce more risk into the system. If you create a two part position then you're averaging the risk. It would be just as effective as playing a single exit point for all lots that was equal to the average risk of looking for maybe 30 pips on the first lot and 80 pips on the second. Thats a decision that has to be made by each trader though. Anyways, evolving into a price action system with trendlines. Is that so bad? This was using one SL,TP, and trigger over all the years. Your results may vary. So if you are going to use the weekly idea then you should probably always be shifting the numbers over time. Only use a year or two worth of data and update the numbers week by week. Unfortunately that means you're only using 52 - 104 candles worth of data. Not sure how reliable it would be. The long time frame might be enough to give it reliability though. Anyways, I am probably going to abandon it for the reasons I'm discussing now. I can do the same thing, irregardless of a time frame, correctly pick areas of S/R and probably increase my success rate. You say average out till you can get out. Do you mean using the martingale method to add to your losing position since eventually the price will retrace? Sure it works so long as your bank roll is huge. The other idea is like I said of immediately entering a reverse position once you are stopped out. I'd rather double up on the next trade though. Martingale method involves placing trades to fight the current trend your already losing against. I'd rather get out, reset the system, then find the trend more accurately again. See the difference? The idea of waiting for the 200 pips though is to prevent you from being placed in a ranging or reversing market. If you institute an always in system then there is just as much a chance of the play turning on you once you enter the reverse position. When you are out of the market and wait for it to absolutely move in one direction then you reduce your risk in that manner tremendously. Sure, maybe its only 50 pips after a 200 pip move. (BTW I'm thinking a 150 pip move might be sufficient. Need to play with it.) I have asked a couple times, but received no answer. How many pips does one need to be considered trading a successful system? I've read threads about "10 pips a day to success" and other such ideas. Trading the simple system of doubling up after losing trades and waiting for 200 pips to take 50 produced 100 pips a month from 7/12-9/11. This is far from averaging 10 pips a day, but its a start. I'll post a chart later to show how my new ideas would be traded as well as a year or two worth of manual 2 hour chart backtesting. How much will using hindsight to find peak/valleys work? Should we look for 100 TP? 50 TP? I'd love to be able to say taking 100 TP is consistent, because if we can do that and double up after the losers then we're trading it such that our account is as if the last trade was also successful. With a 50 TP 100SL we'd need to triple up after a losing trade to make it seem as if the losing trade actually profited. Up to the trader and their bank account really. The problem that may arise from the daily/weekly strategy is that its being curve fit. If its constantly updated, can it last? I'm not sure. I'm only leaning in this direction because there is no need for excel spreadsheets to find equilibrium points. It's simple add/subtract from current price levels. Monitor the charts to find peaks/valleys. And with less work it could actually prove more effective since it finds support/resistance which are disregarded in the daily and weekly range strategies. I'm trying to play the same system, but simpler and more effective. Isn't that what we're looking for? Matt

--- 帖子 #550 ---
If we're talking about the same thing there is a difference. If you're averaging the trade, i.e. using the martingale method, then you've lost the original trade and want to add to that position to bring your average price closer to the current price such that on a retrace you're likely to go in profit. Thats up to you to do. Every trader should determine what exit strategies and methods they're comfortable with and can use with their bank account. The problem is needing large bankrolls if it doesn't retrace. I also don't like the idea that you see that it's a losing trade yet the strategy involves adding more positions to predict a retracement. You're fighting the trend. I'd rather get out of the market to allow a new chart setup to materialize so that I can try to position myself in the trend again. If I know my trades are 70% accurate I'd rather bet on the next trade to double up since my system has no accuracy at predicting where the market will turn. It might be sooner than you think at waiting for 200 pips too. Say you waited 200 pips from 1.8800 and entered long at 1.9000 to exit at 1.9050. It hits a 100 SL at 1.8900. Most instances involve the turn in momentum to take place over time. There's a flat spot at the top of the chart showing resistance. So you enter a new order to enter a trade 200 pips from the high of that run. Most likely the original trade didn't turn against you as soon as it hit 1.9000. We'll say it ran to 1.9025. So if your trade gets stopped out you know the peak of that run was 1.9025 and to enter a sell order at 1.8825. When you get stopped out on the original trade price would have had to hit 1.8900 so you're only 75 pips away from entering the next trade to double up on. That shouldn't take very long to trigger. Yes this system does work for any price on a chart. Set a price, wait 200 pips, enter and TP 50. This is what the new posts to this thread are discussing right now. I first introduced the idea that waiting for new candles and resetting the system isn't necessary and could actually hurt this system. I'm trying to present the idea instead that we should take a simple look at a chart to use the highs and lows of the peak/valleys as our points to straddle. How many ranging markets or bad trades resulting from hitting S/R can we eliminate by not basing our positions on a time frame and more on the actual price of the market? You might have to work with the charts to accomplish 400 pips per month. That can be quite a lot of pips. Looking for more pips introduces more risk into the system. If I can get 150-250 pips a month to compound I'll be happy. Eventually by trading more lots I'll be able to get the same profit at 50 pips as I would trading a single lot for 100. That's up to you, again, to decide. I'll end by noting the idea of using the highs/lows of runs has a built in safety device. Most likely prices don't stall out on 1.9000 or 1.8400; even numbers. This means when we place our orders off of them it could automatically protect us from placing orders and SL's at levels that could get stop hunted. Whats 200 pips from 1.8847? 1.8647. Whats 150 pips from 1.8847? 1.8697. This gives us a little more peace of mind knowing it makes it easy for us to avoid being part of a typical trades mindset and entering trades at round numbers like 1.8650 or 1.8700. Matt

Ok doke. I'm going to attach a picture below of how my new idea would play out. Since I was looking at 2 months of data, 7/11-9/11, I had to compress the chart. Therefore I couldn't put text on it. I'll explain by arrow colors. First yellow arrow - on this chart this would be the first level to base a trigger off of. Since this is a peak it means we base sell trigger off of this number. That would be 1.8476-200 = 1.8247 which is marked by the second yellow arrow and a TP 50 is marked by the bottom yellow arrow. If we played the trade perfectly we could have banked 92 pips if we let the trade run. (not worth it IMO compared to the potential los on other trades.) Green arrow marks the new low. This is where we base our buy trigger 200 pips from. 2nd arrow is the trigger, 3rd is the TP. As you can see the price continued upwards for another 150-200 pips. I've been trying to think of ways to trade continuing trends. Right now I'm looking at looking for the retrace to see where the new base forms. Use that as the new low to base the buy trigger off of. In this instance that point is marked by the white arrow at 1.8414. So the trigger is 1.8616. That continued uptrend did not reach that point so no trigger was hit and I would have cancelled it. Red arrow designates new high formed in that trend at 1.8597. Sell trigger is then shown by second red arrow at 1.8397. This trade would have ended in loss. That same candle to trigger the losing trade would later be our point to base our long trigger off of. The point was 1.8383 shown by turqoise arrow. Next turqoise arrow is the trigger and then the next is TP 50 point. The high off of that trend did not go down 200 pips to trigger anything. So we find the low to continue the trend. This is shown by the yellow arrow at 1.8543. Trigger at 1.8743 and TP at 1.8793. Uptrend continues, no sell triggers. Look for new low to base buy trigger. This point marked by green arrow at 1.8699. Trigger at 1.8899 with TP at 8949. I would not have made a new trade since the upmove was in only one candle and would be too volitile to judge. There was no new low to base a buy trigger off of. As time passes by on the chart you will place your triggers off of different points and change it accordingly. So the candle after the big run up formed a high for several candles. Then later a higher high was formed and that would be the new point to base the trigger off of. It was a high of 1.9144 designated by the white arrow. Trigger is 1.8944 with TP at 1.8894. This is where things get rough for the system. The market ranges drastically. It stays out for most of the time and then finally the moves are so violent that it allows a trigger to be hit. We base a long trigger off the low designated by the red arrow. Price is 1.8775, trigger is 1.8975 and TP 1.9025. As you can see the market hits our trigger and then reverses hard. Hindsight shows the market will range for quite a bit longer. So there is the 2nd losing trade. The next trade designated by the turqoise would have been a tough one that could have gone either way. The base was 1.8828, trigger 1.9028 and TP at 1.9078. The market went to 1.9027 and then dropped 131 pips. We would have narrowly missed a loss by 1 pip. This could have gone either way really. We lucked out in this situation. That would have been 2 losing trades in a row. This is why I say doubling up on trades may not be for everyone. To break even on the last 2 trades you'd need to put four times your usual size into the next play since you had doubled up on the last one as well. Anyways, next trade is profitable anyways. This is why I say I like the idea of doubling up on the next trade. If the system is very successful then I will trust eventually things will work out. It may be rough if you're unwisely using large lot sizes to play with for every trade. If you only use 2% per trade you would of had to use 4%, 8%, 16%, 32%, and 64% depending on if you lose that many in a row. I think this system is very unlikely to hit 5 trades in a row that lose. The next trade is shown by the yellow arrows. High is 1.9091. Trigger at 1.8891 and TP at 1.8841. SUCCESS! Last trade for this time period is the last set of green arrows. High of 1.8869 for a sell trigger at 1.8669 and TP at 1.8619. Another successful trade. The last white arrow is just showing the current point where we're basing our long trigger off of. Its the low of that valley. I like using this time period to show how survivable this system could be. We had a long period of ranging. This is a 2 hour chart. It ranged in the middle there for 18 days! That's a long time to be stuck in the same 150-200 pips. So lets look at the results. 9 winning trades versus 2 losing trades. For 2 months of time that equates to 350 pips profit or 175 pips a month. If you had tripled up on losers to breakeven on the loss as well as make 50 profit then it would have been like having 11 winning trades of 550 pips or 275 pips per month. The problem is if you were to get unlucky and had lost those two trades in a row where we luckily missed out by 1 pip. In that case you would have to triple up on your triple up to make those trades seem like profit, or 9 times your typical entry size to hope the third trade wins. I hope I've explained all of this clearly to everyone. I'll be backtesting further, but wanted to get a chart on here for people to see. Time to discuss. http://img295.imageshack.us/img295/8574/200piphh0.png

--- 帖子 #559 ---
I should have clarified. The results I give are if you double up after the loser. This is because I trust the system to be much more right than it is wrong. So when you double it up, instead of losing on one trade and winning on the next, -100 +50 = -50, it actually loses on one and wins double on the next, -100 + 100 = 0. So a losing trade just cancels out a winning trade. 11 trades - 9 wins, 2 losses. So the total profit is actually just like having only 7 wins. So 50 X 7 = 350 pips for the two months. 175 pips per month. Sorry I didn't clarify that earlier. For these months it would have produced 450-200 = 250 or 125 pips a month if you decided to not double up. Not as good, but not terrible for literally looking at a chart for maybe 2 minutes out of a day.

--- 帖子 #563 ---
Yea, I know watching it can be a pain in the butt and very nerve racking. It's what prevents a lot of people from going pro with trading. They just can't handle themselves. I've done some more backtesting. I assumed that the periods I was previously testing on were prime conditions for the system. (Even though we all know they weren't really.) So I tried to break the system. I set my chart to daily and backed it off so I could get the big picture of the last 2 years of trading. From what I saw, the period from February 1, 2006 to about April 15th, 2006 would be the absolute worst case scenerio for this trending/breakout system. It was ranging in between 1.7230 and 1.7630 at the extremes and included many smaller oscillations in between. There are other periods of ranging, such as from late August 2004 to mid-october 2004, but they wouldn't be as bad as the period I tested. You can clearly see in the 2004 period that it did have a pursuasion to the upside even while ranging. Anyways, what are the results for 2/1/2006-4/15/2006? It was rough. VERY ROUGH. You'll need some massive guts to be able to trade this system people. There were 16 trades made. 9 were winners and 7 were losers. Thats not the rough part. The rough part is that there was a losing streak of 3. This is why I want to explain my preference for doubling up on losing trades. If I had simply accepted the losses for losses and not doubled up my profits would be: 50 X 9 = 450. My losses would be: -100 X 7 = -700. So 450 + (-700) = -250. Now what happens when I double up on my trades after losses to overcome them? Well since I had consecutive losses, one win on the next trade after the 3 would make up for all 3 losses. So it wouldn't leave me with only 2 of the 9 trades profiting. The problem is we're risking quite a bit. Say we risk 2% of our account on a typical trade. We lose the first and double up on the second. Second loses and double up on the third. Third loses and double up on the fourth. Fourth wins. HOORAY. THANK YOU GOD! You would have risked the following amounts of your account on the trades. 2% - 4% - 8% - 16%. You can see whats happening. Do you have the guts to do that? What does this do for our profits though? Well because we're only doubling up and are trying to breakeven on the losses it doesn't add any profits when we finally win after the losses. It does get rid of the -250 pip loss though. I'm happy about that. So if you had doubled up after each loss, including the consecutive losses, you would have made 200 pips in profit for the 2.5 months. Theres a big difference between +200 and -250, wouldn't you say? This just gives me more confidence in trading this type of system. This was obviously a terrible situation for the system, but through wise money management you can easily turn a bad situation into a good one. I would not expect this system to have more than 4 consecutive losses in a row. Even if the system had 2 sets of 3 consecutive losses in a month it would be able to survive them so long as there was a win in between them to bring your account back to even. Anyways, I thought I'd post all of that for you to show that this system can perhaps survive even the toughest trading scenerios. I didnt want to be looking through rose colored glasses considering the great trading gbp/usd has been having this last month or two. Please, I encourage you all to manually backtest this and demo forward test before trying it live. I would really appreciate as much criticism, opinions, or tips. I'll be testing more periods to see if I was wrong in thinking I had found the worst case scenerio. Matt

There was then a spinning top candle and then another severe drop in price in the next candle. I took the high off the spinning top to base my 200 pip sell trigger off of. It ended in a losing trade. Ouch. 2% - 4% - 8% - 16% - 32% risked on the doubling up trades with the 32% winning. When you get periods of time like this you almost want the losers to be in a row. This is because using this risky doubling down strategy you cover your losses with only one win. If the losers were not consecutive then you would be using one winner per loser to breakeven on the losses. So 12 wins - 8 losses = -200 without utilizing a double down strategy. -100 if you didn't take the first trade. Using a doubling down on losers strategy you would be +450 for the 3 months. It seems this strategy seems to be averaging anywhere from 125-400 pips a month. I'm backtesting under absolute terrible trading conditions of the tightest ranges. I'm thinking though, that it is nearly almost absolutely profitable only because of the risks involved with doubling down. Without doubling down this strategy would produce several periods of losses. Possible ideas to prevent yourself from having to produce 4 losses in a row would be to expand the trigger to 300 pips so that price is most likely moving out of the range it's currently in. It brings up the idea though, does it matter how good the system is if we're willing to risk our money in certain money management strategies? --- 帖子 #578 ---
That was somewhat the original idea of the thread. Instead of previous session highs and lows we used the open price. Some have profited off of this strategy. What I didn't like was the system resests itself only because of time and a new candle forming. My idea right now is to disregard time and only play off of the highs and lows of the runs we see on intraday charts. If the low of a run was 1.9600 than play the breakout when it rises 200 pips even if thats 2 or 3 days down the road. Whats your opinion on that instead of resetting the system for each new session? Also, I'm not so sure your strategy would work in theory. If you place a trigger so many pips away from the highs and lows from a previous session it will be hard to determine the buffer for each session. There will be candles that close near their high and then there will be candles that have closed 40 pips away from the high. So a sell trigger should not be based off of the high because the next candle could be only 5 pips away and create a triger off of a weak trend. The only way to use that idea, IMO, would be to base buy triggers off of highs and sell triggers off of lows. This again has the problem of resetting itself after each candle though. The price could move in a strong, predictable downtrend but stay inside the buffer you've created from the highs and lows. It could maybe only move down 40 pips a day and your trigger is at 50 pips. No trade this candle. It does the same thing next candle and doesn't trigger again. The price has moved 80 pips, but no trigger hit. That's why I say we should eliminate time from the equation and play the highs and lows of the trends instead of resetting the system after each candle. Matt

--- 帖子 #582 ---
It's not technically martingale. Martingale is when you add to your already losing position and expect price to turn. Your lowering/raising your average price so it's easier to make a profit on the retrace that you are hoping for. My strategy involves exiting the market to double up on the next trade knowing that my strategy is more than 50% correct. I'd rather give myself a shot at being right on another trade rather than try to turn a losing trade around. For a 100 SL and 50 TP I would need to triple up on the investment to make it seem as if I was profiting even in the losing trades. I'm only looking to break even right now so my losers don't eat into my profits. So really my risk would be 1-2-4-8 to break even on the losing trades. It's not to win just one either. If on a 3 consecutive loss series where I would risk 1-2-4 and then win on the fourth trade I would actually be winning 6. (-100) + (-100) + (-100) = -300. To break even I'd need to win 6 trades that profit +50 pips each. So in one trade I'm really winning 6 trades. Like I said, this strategy isn't for everyone and will not survive if you're not managing your money correctly. This is where a highly leveraged account can be a plus. With less margin required you can put more trades towards a certain goal. If you know your strategy is more than 50% successful then you can rest assured that eventually you'll be at breakeven, if not profit. Eventually when my account grows large enough I will triple up on each losing trade to make it 1-3-9-27. Those are lot sizes, not percentage of account. This way when I know I'll be winning eventually then it'll be like profiting on every trade. 20 trades in 2 months = 300 pips a month irregardless if 5 or 6 of those 20 are losers. A large account will be necessary for this. Anyways, ROI. Even if the strategy only gives you 100 pips a month it is still a good ROI when compared to typical investments. If you put 2% of your account towards each trade then 100 pips a month is 2% ROI I believe; 24% in a year. There aren't many investments offering that kind of ROI. I've already shown that 100 pips a month seems to be a lowball number for when the market isn't trending well. Is there something I'm missing? Matt

--- 帖子 #584 ---
Wouldn't that be (-100) + (-200) + (-400) on three losing trades? If you are doubling up, you need to keep doubling up your loses too. You'd also have to go for the same profit/loss targets, at a bare minimum.. If you are onto your fourth loss, and you do "win", you would have gained 50 pips x 8, or 400 total pips. By this time, you have lost 700 pips. A very high risk way of trading. Even if you have a strategy that is 100tp/100sl, and wins 55% of the time. Who says you can't lose 10 times in a row? It is _unlikely_, but it is _possible_. I use to use the same concept while playing Black Jack. As I lost, double the bet. You'd think you couldn't lose more than 5 or 6 times in a row. It happens all the time though. The better way to play Black Jack is to do progressive winning. As you win, every other time, increase your bet. 1 1, 2 2, 4 4, etc... Would I ever use this method in trading? Never. Take the bumps with the bruises.... Once a trade takes profit or a loss, that trade is done, onto the next one... That is where your money management comes into play. As long as your risk to reward ratio is good (1.5 at least, better in the 2.0 or 3.0 range), then it doesn't really matter what happened the last trade. I personally watched this thread much closer in the beginning. The original methods posted do work (I personally like the 20/-20 straddle of London open). Sure, they have their bad days, but they have good days in return. Lately, too many untested _theories_ have been thrown out, many off track from a "daily break-out" approach... Be nice to see the thread get back on that track daily break-out strategies.

High leverage also helps out in this situation to keep margin calls down. You just have to be smart with it. Are 8 losing trades in a row possible? Very much so. What are the chances though? Should we be so afraid of such a chance? If a system is even just 50% successful what are the chances of 8 trades in a row losing? If I remember my college classes correctly, although the chance of the trade losing is 50% on each trade independently, once we try to string them together the chance of such an occurance actually becomes the following: .5 X .5 X .5 X .5 X .5 X .5 X .5 X .5 = .00390625. Correct me if I'm wrong. The chance of 8 losing trades in a row on a 50% system is just .3%. If I think the system is 60% successful, or 40% wrong, the chances of consecutive losing trades is: 2- .16 3- .064 4- .0256 5- .01024 6- .004096 7- .0016384 8- A really small number. So thats why I think the strategy is still viable. With good money management, i.e. - not using lots too large for your account, you can still survive a string of many losses. After 5 losses you can see just how unlikely that gets to be. Are you afraid of losing 100 trades in a row just like you are of losing 2? No, because losing 100 in a row is severely unlikely. Even if you were trying to be wrong you'd still probably win since the market wouldn't let you be 100% right about being wrong. --- 帖子 #596 ---
A little adaptation to the Daily Strategy that this thread has been discussing. It does require an account that allows hedging (I use interbankfx). At 00:00 GMT buy and sell the EUR/USD with a 50 pip stop loss and 15 trailing stop. Close out all open orders between 23:30 and 24:00 GMT. The premise of this trade is to capitalize on the interday price activity. If you look at a candle chart most days will have shadows of at least 17 pips on the bottom if an up day and on the top if a down day. In these cases you'll have a profitable trade on BOTH trades. However, days when there are shawdows of less than 17 pips you lose (most of the times it is the whole 50 but somedays it will only be in the 30-40 range). You will incur some days of losing 50 pips but the gains definitely offset those times. Here are the results from April to October: April +458 May +184 June -3 July +333 August +573 September -35 October +140 Total Gain +1650 I'm currently running Novembers numbers. As for December it is currently up +175 pips. Q

--- 帖子 #602 ---
QMG, I'm afraid this won't work in reality (forward trading) because the trailing stops don't work that way. What you are doing is setting the stop to BE when the trade is 15 pips up and calling it a trailing stop.. In reality, a trailing stop of 15 would begin when the trade reaches 15 pips in the correct direction and begins to pull the stop loss along with it. So, the trade could easily go the 17 pips you mentioned, then reverse the other direction and still lose 48 pips (stop was pulled along 2 pips), not be stopped for a small gain. I think over time in forward trading the spreads would simply eat all profits. I have been looking for YEARS for an effective way to hedge trades and still make some sort of profit. Still haven't found it.

--- 帖子 #603 ---
Yes, this is the old hedge hog revisited. The problem is the draw down when you do get stung by the stop losses. Just do a search for Hedge Hog and you will see what this is...

Assuming your above scenario--lets say the price started at 1.3200 and moved up to 1.3217 and reversed 48 pips to 1.3169. Based upon my "system/theory" you would make 2 pips on the BUY side and have 14 pips "locked in" on the SELL side. If the market when back to the open price the sell order would get stopped out at 1.3284 This works because Interbankfx allows you to take both positions at 1.3200 with a 15 pip trailing stop. On interbankfx the trailing stop is a true trailing stop (unlike fxcm ) that locks in the profit once the price has moved 15 pips and then moves pip for pip after that, e.g. moves the the stop loss to break even once the 15 pip trailing stop is achieved. --- 帖子 #616 ---
Yes, however, be careful because there isn't a pip for pip correlation. With the tight Trailing Stop of only 15 pips you can be stopped out well before realizing the 80 pip gain. In a steady, straight forward market it works like that but when its choppy you get stopped out quite often during a 30 minute candle because of the price movement therein. Earlier in this thread you will find discussion re: the 50 pip SL. From my memory it seems that once the price has moved that far the chance of it retracing back to the other side of the open is drastically reduced. It is a money management thing. Q

In my accout I bought the EUR/USD and then immediately after I sold the EUR/USD--both with 15 Trailing Stops and a Stop Loss of 50. Currently, I'm up 5 pips on the BUY and down 5 on the SELL. Q

--- 帖子 #622 ---
Most brokers don't let you buy and sell the same pair (ie: hedge/go both ways). Then, on some, like FXCM , they don't trail the same. On IBFX, if you have a 15 PIP trailing stop, at a +15 PIPs, your stop would be moved to 0. If you are +16 PIPs, then the SL is moved to +1. If you move +50, then your SL is set to +35. At least that is my understanding. Am playing around with this in a demo at IBFX. David

--- 帖子 #640 ---
To anybody wanting to try this strategy using Interbankfx make sure your computer system doesn't go into hibernation. To turn off your hibernation mode right click on your start up screen, go to properties, on the screen saver tab towards the bottom you'll see a Power...button, click on that button which will bring you to the power schemes page. Make sure all options, especially "turn off hard disks", system standby, and system hibernates are switched to "NEVER". By doing this your Trailing Stops will be active with interbank. Last night my computer went into hibernation and my Trailing Stops weren't activated because as far as Interbankfx is concerned, and their servers, my computer was off. They don't store the Trailing Stops on their server but go off of yours. Fortunately, I was able to break even for the day and not lose anything. Unfortunately I left 86 pips on the table A lesson well learned!!! Hope this helps... Q

Here is an idea I am playing with and will be backtesting this weekend. At 5 PM EST (00:00 on FXDD) open a trade in the direction of the previous day's candle. Set TP for 40 and SL for 20. --- 帖子 #663 ---
This is not directly related to your strategy, but I noticed that all of your orders (entry, limit, stop) were numbers ending in zero. One sure way to get stopped out is to set your order parameters with numbers ending with zero or five. The big dogs love to take out stops because they know that newbies frequently use numbers divisable by 5 or 10. So add 3 or 4 to your entry or exit parameters and you will probably be more successful.

--- 帖子 #669 ---
Brett... you are more or less following Micardo's original plan for Daily Range strategy. You don;'t need an EA. Here's how I do it. Every day at 5PM EST (22:00 GMT) FXDD gives a new daily candle. I check the opening price on that candle and place my orders. I place a buy stop 55 pips above the open price and also set my stop loss and take profit levels. I also place a sell stop for 50 pips below the open price and set my take profit and stop loss points. I like to place two trades each direction, with differing take profit levels. I also set a trailing stop on the second trade but try to let in run to 60 or 80 pips. All this is possible on Metatrader free of charge from brokers like F X D D or I B F X. Even when I trade with I B F X I use the F X D D charts to get their daily candle, as I B F X issues their daily candle at 7 PM EST (00:00). I spend 10 minutes making lots of trades like this and then forget about it (sort of ) until the next morning. So far Micardo's method is positive for about the last 6 weeks or so. Rather rocky in December though. Good luck. This is NOT to be confused with the interesting QMG method which places market orders in two different directions at 00:00 GMT.

So then you entered 2 standard 100,000 lots on each trigger? Have you looked at the days you missed to see if you would have profited or lost? It looks like you missed many days. I still don't know how accurate these results are though. This month span was obvisously great for trending systems. I'd be careful about continuing at that size unless your account can handle it. How'd it feel to lose $2100 just like that on the 7th and 11th? I'm not sure why you lost on those days though, GFT is showing nicely trending days. Perhaps our times are set up differently. Something to look at is that you never lost on a trade without losing on both. When you add up the wins on the 2nd lot that you let ride, it averages out to 28.6 pips, even with the big 60 and 80 pip profits. Looking at your rules again, how did you get the 80 pips on the 22nd of November? So you would have been better just exiting both lots at the 30 pip point. The average profit on the 2nd lot was 28.6 pips and that's with the 80 pip day. If you make that a 60 pip day then the average on the 2nd lot is 27.3 pips. If you had just exited at 30 pips on the 2nd lot that would be 2.6 pips per trade more. 2.6 X 15 winning trades = 40 pips = $400 more in your pocket. That's an easy 9 percent increase in profits right there. This is why I tried to analyze the data from excel the way I did weeks ago. You probably would have blown the results you got out of the water if you had simply exited all trades after a 35 pip move on both lots. I still say there is an efficient point for each trading day rather than exiting at multiple points. Looking at your figures again I am confused some more. You have a 30 pip trailing stop on the second lot. How did you exit some of them at 38 pips profit, or $380 profit? That would have to mean price would have moved to +68 pips and then drop the 30 back to only 38 pips profit. The same goes for many of the 330 pip days. I'll have to assume that since you took an 800 pip profit that you didnt follow your rules discreetly. Again, thats why I explored this strategy through excel. I believe there is one efficient point. Unfortunately it means we allow more losers and right now with a 30 TP and 50/55SL it means we lose more than what we win. When you lose you lose big. The 7th and 11th total losses are almost half of your total profits. Imagine if you had caught another two days like that. I've been debating setting a TP/SL for myself in my trendline trading system of TP 75 SL 50 just to allow for the noise and also win more than when I lose. But hey, you can't complain about $4480 bucks in your pocket off of little work right? That's a nice living if the system is that consistent.

--- 帖子 #690 ---
going for 70 to prevent more than 4 in a row failures (2003 caused more than 4) 2003 = 1661 2004 = 1942 2005 = 2325 2006 = 1981 going for 85 and exclude 2003. 2004 = 2587 2005 = 3395 2006 = 3356 You might think you could increase pip target each year since 2003 could only get 70, but going for more than 85 in 2005 caused 5 in a row failure. I try to prevent this because of doubling up. Using mini-lots you buy 1 lot, then 2, then 4, then 8 but because 4 can fail in a row the next one has to be 16 lots, which in my testing always won. I would not be comfortable buying 32 lots or 64 lots so that is why I limited it to 4 losses. Of course allowing 5 in a row resulted in huge profits though. Another idea would be using the 115 wait, 70, 60s/l just as a guide and wait for 4 in a row to fail (or 1,2, or 3) before starting, and knowing the next trade will most likely win and buying 10 lots or whatever. I included this as an option in my program and here are the total results 2003 - 2006 going for 70 and waiting til 4 fail in a row = 350 pips. Multiply by 10 lots = 3500 (only happened 5 times) 2004 - 2006 going for 85 and waiting til 4 fail in a row = 340 pips X 10 lots = 3400 (only happened 4 times and if you kept it at 70 it only happened twice which netted 140) I should also say these are net pips. I deducted my 5 pip spread on the pound already.

--- 帖子 #691 ---
I would suggest not bothering with martingale in this strategy, or almost any strategy. It works, yes, but look what you've done. You can only trade 1 minilot to be able to martingale on the trades following it. I think the profits would add up greater if you just risked 1 standard lot on each trade and took the larger wins/losses, but didn't try to cover the losses. Get what I'm saying? If your account can handle trading a standard lot then do that rather then only play for 1 minilot wins. Its just not worth it. Here is the minimum martingale risk for consecutive losses and allow yourself to only breakeven at the end. 1 -1 -2 - 4 - 8. So on the 5th trade you've already lost 8% of your account and risking 8% on the last trade. The losses could be 16% of your account and then it only gets uglier from there. To avoid huge losses you use the minilots and your account grows slowly. A lot of risk for such slow growth. Lame. Anyways, are those pip totals including martingaling or not? Something to consider also. You mentioned your idea of waiting for the 4 losses in a row. What about waiting for 4 wins in a row and then taking the trade opposite what is signaled? How many times did it win 4 times in a row. You could essentially double your pip totals right there. Matt

Firstly I’d like to say thankyou to Micardo and MarkJ for their inspiration and contribution. The trading plans below were originally based upon MarkJ’s plan, so respect to him.&lt;?xml:namespace prefix = o ns = "urn:schemas-microsoft-com:office:office" /&gt;&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; My thoughts on the DRS (daily range strategy) is that the objective of the strategy is to find a point in price and time where GBP takes sustainable direction to trigger the TP’s with an acceptable level of volatility and drawdown. &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; The Big Ben paper indicates GBP trades lightly in the Asian session, which is able to be seen on the chart. The GBP has two major trading sessions being the UK and US sessions. There is a tendency for price to consolidate prior to the open of both sessions and to take direction shortly after the open. I’ve noticed that the trend established from UK open doesn’t necessarily persist through the US open. For instance a news release at US open can revert a trend. I’ve also noticed direction seems to weaken after the UK close. So the two periods in time I’m interested in trading is from UK open to US open and US open to UK close. I’ve taken the view of trading these sessions discretely, that is, to close any open positions at US open rather than risk price hitting the TSL upon news or trend reversion.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; I’ve back tested several derivations of the plans below over a randomly selected three week period which included both trending and non-trending price action. I tested 3 different SL systems:1) stop set at 20 pips and not moved – lost pips, 2) 20 pip TSL which engages when price moves 20 pips – lost pips 3) 20 pip TSL which starts to trail immediately upon entry – made pips. &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; My current broker doesn’t offer TSL’s, but that is not a problem. Can anyone recommend a broker that offers a TSL that trails immediately, MT4, preferably 3 pip spread and they reckon they are ok? &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; I tested two strangles 20 pip and 25 pip. There wasn’t much difference between them however the 25 pip was a little better. It would be worth testing both over a larger sample size to see if it changes the result. To address JillyB’s comment about the significance of round numbers, I think it has an effect on instruments traded on centralised exchanges, I’m not sure that that holds true with instruments traded OTC. I think different data feeds and spreads would confound this issue. Heh, it has been hard enough to even establish when London opens due to time zones and DST. When I was back testing I didn’t notice a higher frequency of entry and revert due to the round numbers.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; My view on multiple TP’s is that each plan (as in Entry, TP &amp; SL) should hold it’s own weight individually and can be combined to smooth the equity curve and profit multiple times from one event. Originally I tested the 4 TP’s with the expectation of dropping the weakest, however they are all profitable so I didn’t see a good reason to drop any of them. In order of most profitable to least 80, 50, 30, 14. I think it was more difficult for the higher win/loss ratio to compensate for the lower profit/loss ratio caused by the 20 SL. I haven’t tested it, however I think moving the 14 to a 20 TP may increase the profitability by balancing the profit/loss ratio.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; Enough yabba, here are the plans.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; Trav UK 25 DRS v1 &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; Place a 4 entry strangle at UK open , 25 pips away from UK open price.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; TP: Target Profit levels are 14, 30, 50, 80 pips away from entry.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; TSL: A 20 pip trailing stop loss which is initiated at entry is applied to all positions.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; TS: A timed stop is also applied so all positions are closed at US open .&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; Close the position when TP, TSL or TS is triggered. &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; This is not an OCO order.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; There is no re-entry.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; Trav US 25 DRS v1 &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; Place a 4 entry strangle at US open , 25 pips away from US open price.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; TP: Target Profit levels are 14, 30, 50, 80 pips away from entry.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; TSL: A 20 pip trailing stop loss which is initiated at entry is applied to all positions.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; TS: A timed stop is also applied so all positions are closed at UK close .&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; Close the position when TP, TSL or TS is triggered. &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; This is not an OCO order.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; There is no re-entry.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; So how did they do over the 3 week sample?&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; UK 20: 247 pips&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; UK 25: 287 pips&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; US 20: -142 pips&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; US 25: -109 pips&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; These figures are net (3 pip spread).&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; Every trading plan is a balance. I’m happy with the result of the UK 25. I think the US plan still has merit, just need to find the right combination for instance maybe a 30 or 35 strangle with perhaps a lesser TP. More work needed.&lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; &lt;o &gt;&lt;/o &gt; I really think this strategy needs to be tested over a longer time period before going live to negate any biases caused by a small sample size. Once the buy and sell entry was placed, I stepped away from the computer except at the appropriate time the next day. Once a buy or sell was executed, I let it run its course. Thanks Mikhail and you were so fast. I have to admit time conversions and DST drive me crazy. There is a link to a pretty good conversion clock under &lt;TABLE cellSpacing=0 cellPadding=0 border=0&gt;&lt;TBODY&gt;&lt;TR vAlign=bottom&gt;&lt;TD&gt; http://www.forexfactory.com/forexfor...bits_start.gif &lt;/TD&gt;&lt;TD&gt; &lt;/TD&gt;&lt;TD width="100%"&gt; Forex Forums &gt; Forex Discussion &lt;/TD&gt;&lt;/TR&gt;&lt;TR&gt;&lt;TD class=navbar style="FONT-SIZE: 12pt; PADDING-TOP: 1px" colSpan=3&gt; http://www.forexfactory.com/forexfor..._finallink.gif &lt;!-- google_ad_section_start --&gt;Dedicated Clock for International Forex Markets. &lt;/TD&gt;&lt;/TR&gt;&lt;/TBODY&gt;&lt;/TABLE&gt; DST will effect the backtesting of this strategy. Here are the conditions: From the last Sunday in October through the last Saturday in March standard time in the United States of America and other European countries is noted as Central Standard Time (CST), (EST), (MST) or (PST). During summer, that is, from the last Sunday in March through the Last Saturday in October, daylight savings time is noted as Central Daylight Time (CDT), (EDT), (MDT) or (PDT) which is one hour added to standard time. So to convert EDT to GMT, just add four(4) hours. Below is a summary of the conversions, this time converting GMT to EST or PST. &lt;TABLE style="WIDTH: 224pt; BORDER-COLLAPSE: collapse" height=100 cellSpacing=0 cellPadding=0 width=300 border=0 x:str&gt;&lt;COLGROUP&gt;&lt;COL style="WIDTH: 56pt; BORDER-LEFT: black 0.5pt solid; WIDTH: 112pt; BORDER-BOTTOM: #ece9d8; HEIGHT: 27pt; BACKGROUND-COLOR: #ffffcc" width=150 colSpan=2 height=36&gt; Eastern Standard Time (EST) &lt;/TD&gt;&lt;TD class=xl22 style="BORDER-RIGHT: #ece9d8;
