Central European Summer Time (CEST) &lt;/TD&gt;&lt;TD class=xl26 style="BORDER-RIGHT: #ece9d8; BORDER-TOP: #ece9d8; BORDER-LEFT: black 0.5pt solid; WIDTH: 112pt; BORDER-BOTTOM: #ece9d8; BACKGROUND-COLOR: #ffffcc" width=150 colSpan=2&gt; GMT + 2 hours = CEST &lt;/TD&gt;&lt;/TR&gt;&lt;/TBODY&gt;&lt;/TABLE&gt; The method I used to identify the consolidation and breakout points was to line up 3 weeks of charts and look for similar tendancies amongst the charts. The times I use are: UK 7:00-13:00GMT, US 13:00-18:00GMT Last Sun March to Last Sat Oct (DST) UK 6:00-12:00GMT, US 12:00-17:00GMT Last Sun Oct to Last Sat March The backtesting I conducted was in Sept. I have checked some charts in Nov and the event seems to have moved an hour with the change from DST. Since an OTC market doesn't have an official open it is not surprising that the times I identified are not exactly the same as the generally quoted trading hours. To avoid confusion it would be best to use the times stated above rather than the generally quoted trading hours. Thanks again Mickhail.

--- 帖子 #712 ---
I'm starting to really consider using this strategy on several of the major uncorrelated pairs. The uncorrelated thread in the discussion forum really got me thinking. Adding uncorrelated pairs to your trading really is a form of hedging. It increases the profits, but not the risk. It minimizes drawdown as well. This is because if we know our system to be profitable then the systems will spend more time winning trades than losing them. So to have two uncorrelated pairs losing at the same time is unlikely, but them winning together isn't unhead of. So if one loses, it's likely the other won. So for the day you're more even than down, which makes it more surviveable. The drawdown is more maneagable. It's the law of large numbers. Therefore we could eliminate the problem of getting stuck in a ranging month. What're the chances several uncorrelated pairs range at the same time? Suddenly my interest in all of this is peaked once again. Since it takes about 1 minute to set up trades I can easily see myself trading many pairs like this. I really never thought of multiple pairs as a hedging strategy. Anyone want to take a shot at which pairs we should use and what TP, SL, triggers we should use on them? Matt

The broker I currently use is IG Markets which uses GMT on their time scale. Regardless of the broker, if you convert to GMT and use the times quoted below you should be using the reference points as I did. So technically the times I have used are not the generally accepted open and closing times. They have the effect of opening the position in a consolidation prior to a breakout and trading the directional move of the UK/US trading session. So I would recommend using the quoted times above rather than the generally accepted open and close times. I'm just changing to a faster ISP so will go dark for a few days. Will answer any queries on monday.

PJ, be aware you could be creating a synthetic cross currency trade, which isn't really advisable. eg: +1 GBP/USD, +1 USD/JPY approximately equals a synthetic +2 GBP/JPY I would recommend learning about synthetic positions before attempting this type of trade. You will probably conclude they are unnecessarily complicated. If your main goal is to trade profitably, unnecessary complications will simply make attaining that goal more difficult.

--- 帖子 #717 ---
Here is what I did for back testing the original daily range strategy: I looked on the charts at FXCM and went back to 2003 to the present looking at 1 hr. charts but keying in on only the opening price at 4pm PST which is 00:00 GMT. 1. Step one - I wrote down the opening price 2. I added 50 pips to the opening price to get the entry for a buy 3. I subtracted 50 pips to the opening price to get the entry for a sell. 4. I set a hard 30 pip stop loss and a 30 pip limit to each entry. 5. If a buy or sell was entered, I left the other opposite entry alone without cancelling. 6. If I was stopped out on a buy or sell, I didn't re-enter. 7. If an order was entered and still in play, I let it run until sitting down at my computer at 4pm PST. 8. I looked at each day on hour charts and figured out the entry and whether or not I would of been stopped or not. At the end of the month, I just noted the wins and losses and figured out the difference. Trading 3 standard lots with a $20,000 initial balance would put at risk 90 pips a trade (30 pips X 3 lots). The most losses in a row were 4 during the period of 2003 to the end of 2006. The worst month trading my scenario was - $900.00 and the best was over $13,000. I am still testing and now using a 30 pip trailing stop loss. Tuesday was a huge win with over $4,500 in profit using 3 standard lots. Take a look at the hourly charts. Wednesday a winner too, with $960.00 using a 30 pip trailing stop loss. I used FXCM charts to view back data and I use FXSOLUTIONS to place my entry orders.

Llambert, What is your strategy for this result? is it to enter at 50 pips above or below 00:00 and take 1st profit at 30? In my data analysis you have a 50% chance of the market reaching 70 pips above open (meaning entering at 40 instead of 50) even less for 80. That's will give a breakeven or a little above or below at best. In my data data analysis price also hits 55 above open and then retraces enough for 50 not to be the best entry price from my experience.

can anyone explain the pros &amp; cons of trailing stops to me is it better to use a larger TS when going for larger targets? example: if i bot cable at 1.9500 with a stop of 1.9475 (25 pips) and a trailing stop of 50 pips after a 50 pip movment what would my new stop become? greg

--- 帖子 #726 ---
On I B F X your trailing stop would be break even after the 50 pip move in your favor. Then it would be pulled along as you go more in your favor. If you went 70 pips in your favor and then for some reason the market crashed you would be stopped out at a 20 pip win. Not all brokers use this kind of stop but I B F X does.

Kwackers, I looked at your strategy. Basically it's the same i'm using. The diference are the parameters used. This are mine: - Each day i put two STOP ORDERS based on 00:00 GMT OPEN trade of GBPUSD pair. - Enter 58 pips above (buy) or below (sell) OPEN GBPUSD. - Limit 15 pips from enter. - Stop 27 pips from enter. I backtested this parameters from 29/05/2006 to 29/12/2006. And this are de results: 1% double loss (sell and buy). 2% double profit (sell and buy). 62% profit (sell or buy). 15% loss (sell or buy). 19% didn't trade. In 155 trading days the systems returns 834 pips of profit. It represents 27 pips per week. It is not so profitable in pips, buy with a good combination of money management rules, it gives 4756% in the period analized. Starting with an hipotetical balance of USD 250 on may 29, at december 29 you would get 7317 USD. In addition, the sistem is very simple, and you don't need to be in front the charts to much time. Thats are the reasons why i decided to start using this method in my real account: simple and no time demand. The backtest was made without considering fundamental information. But analizing the worst weeks i realized that there isn't a real trend. What i mean it was very tighty. The same that happened today and yesterday with de GBPUSD pair. This kind of days it is better don't trade. I think tomorrow, with USD PPI report, will be a nice day for this method. If you want, i can explain the reasons of the parameters used. I also backtested this parameters: ENTER LIMIT STOP 58 22 25 58 27 27 56 60 38 56 40 30 56 50 100 56 110 100 I hope this help all of us. Regards,

Kwackers, 27 pips p/wk is a marginal profit. I hope that figure is net otherwise spread will blow it out of the water. You will need to achieve a win/loss of around 80% for a trade with a 15TP and 30SL to be profitable. Hope you are running a TSL on the 80TP cause it is a lot of profit to give away if price reverts after entry. Best of luck. Traderone, We actually need directional/trending movement rather than volatility. The whipsaws and generally non-directional movement challenge the profitability of this system. My latest thoughts are: the most profitable days are when the market shows strong direction. The least profitable days are when the market is volatile and whipsaws around taking out both entries and SL's. On a non-trending day I have a good chance of the 14TP being triggered, however it is very unlikely that the 50 or 80TP will meet its target so my thought about refining the strategy is to apply the larger TP's (eg 50TP &amp; 80TP) on trending days and do not apply them on non-trending days. This bodes the question what is a good indicator to determine what is a trending v's non-trending day. Then would the indicator be sophisticated enough to switch on the TP's depending upon the strength of the trend. For instance: non-trending=14TP, slight trend=14 &amp; 30TP, trending=14, 30 &amp; 50TP, strong trend=14, 30, 50 &amp; 80TP. I haven't explored this further at this stage. If anyone can suggest an indicator it would be appreciated. Good to hear from you Micardo.

--- 帖子 #753 ---
Hi Mikhail. I've been thinking of some ways of developing the DRS EA further. I haven't written MQ4 before, so any help would be appreciated, but if not, would you mind posting the MQ4 version of your DRS EA so I can continue this project? My current thoughts are to: Stage 1 Optimise it for time and for price targets. A larger first TP, for instance, 20pips may work better than the 14TP because of the difference in the profit/loss ratio. Stage2 Add in Money Mgt such as in Phoenix Stage3 Add code to switch the Entries and TP's on or off depending upon the likelihood of them being sucessfully achieved. The method I have thought of is to look back to the period between the start and end time settings of the previous two days, take the difference between the open and the high of that period over the last two days and average it. If the TP is &gt;= the look back then allow the position to open else exit. Ditto for open and low. These two events should be independent of each other. So for instance, if we are in a strong uptrend all the long positions will be allowed and the short positions will not be allowed. I haven't backtested this theory however I think it should increase the number of positions in a trending market and reduce the number of positions in a nontrending market which should hopefully increase the profitability of the system. Stage4 Allow the money mgt % of free margin (allowed per trade) to be incrementally increased (by a % of free margin) upon consecutive wins up to a ceiling. Each trade should be treated individually. For example, if the Long 30TP consecutively wins the % of free margin per trade gets incremented, however if the Long 50TP doesn't win it doesn't get incremented. This should allow larger positions to be taken when the market is trending or at least when you are consecutively winning for whatever reason. This should increase the profitability of the system. I think this may be in Phoenix as well. I think after completing these stages of development the EA would be really quite powerful. Thankyou in advance.

--- 帖子 #754 ---
At the risk of this thread becoming a monologue. I've been backtesting and optimising the time and price inputs. The methodology I've used is to optimise over 2006 data and test against 2005 data. My view on multiple TP’s is that each plan (as in Entry, TP &amp; SL) should hold it’s own weight individually and can be combined to smooth the equity curve and profit multiple times from one event. So I tested each plan independently. The good news is that after optimisation I produced some fantastic results; TP1 50% ROC, TP2 100% ROC. The bad news is when I tested it against 2005 data it produced a negative result so the strategy for 2006 did not hold true for 2005. This got me thinking - does that mean the methodology of optimising over 1 year doesn't produce a robust result? Does that mean I should ditch that method and try perhaps a rolling optimisation eg: optimise for dec apply to jan, optimise for jan apply to feb etc. Maybe that will help. Then I thought maybe optimising for time and price should be the last stage of development rather than the first. The stages of development mentioned in my previous post will all effect the way this strategy works and the profitability of different inputs. So I think the stages of development need to be completed first. I've noticed the EA is producing OCO orders when the strategy is not meant to enter an OCO order. I've also noticed the trailing stop the EA is using is a trailing profit stop. That is, price needs to move into profit by the quantum of the trailing stop for it to engage. When I conducted my manual backtesting I found that a trailing stop loss which turns into a trailing profit stop was significantly more profitable than a trailing profit stop by itself. That is, a trailing stop which engages immediately when the bid-TSL&gt;SL. Example code below: If TrailingStop &gt; 0 then // if trailing stops are used { If OrderValue(cnt,VAL_STOPLOSS)&lt;(Bid-Point*TrailingStop) then { ModifyOrder(OrderValue(cnt,VAL_TICKET),OrderValue(cnt,VAL_OPENPRICE), Bid-Point*TrailingStop,OrderValue(cnt,VAL_TAKEPROFIT),Red); Exit }; }; After making these changes and completing these stages of development I think we would have a powerfully profitable EA. Mikhail, if your out there, help!!!

--- 帖子 #756 ---
hello again Trav , It is very good to see that you are trying to develop the system for it to become robust but I cant help but comment on a few things if you don't mind. The EA I posted here is not a trading system it is just an expert adviser that makes trading the DRS just a little bit easier by automating the task for you. But if you truly want to make a robust trading system out of this strategy, that would be profitable in the long run I suggest you stop looking at fixed levels of entry and exit, It just will not work. The market is dynamic so your system must also be able to change as the market changes. To achieve this in the DRS you have to look at ATR or percentages. An example would be the "SBS EA". its logic is similar to this system but the levels of entry is not fixed. It bases its entry level by calculatuing 70% of yesterday daily range, then thats where it puts its entry levels. and closes all orders at end of the day no tp. Very simple but proves to be profitable. Also if you are able to make a system profitable both in 2005 and 2006, then you would have found your grail, its because 2005 is mostly ranging while 2006 is mostly trending. Just a few suggestions but I encourage you to continue to look at the market and it will reveal itself to you. Regards, Mikhail

--- 帖子 #771 ---
I have found that when backtested, taking profits has drastically decreased the overall profitability of the system. I have also found that filtering out periods of low volatility (defined as ATR(20) &lt; 130PIPS) is non-beneficial. What I have found is that trading this system on Monday, Tuesday and Thursdays reduces the trade frequency, and increases profits. The only concern I would have about the system when traded mechanically is that there are looooong flat-times. Possibly adding in some style of counter-term trade would help. Inserted Code Inputs: dollarStop(600), expansionPIPS(.008), DOW1(1), DOW2(2), DOW3(5); vars:longTradesToday(0), shortTradesToday(0), switch(0), buyPrice(0), sellPrice(0), longTrailingExit(0), shortTrailingExit(0); If time crosses above Sess1EndTime then begin longTradesToday = 0; shortTradesToday = 0; buyPrice = close + expansionPIPS; sellPrice = close - expansionPIPS; end; if time &gt; Sess1StartTime and (DayOfWeek(Date) = DOW1 or DayOfWeek(Date) = DOW2 or DayofWeek(date) = DOW3) then begin if longTradesToday = 0 and marketPosition &lt;&gt; 1 then buy("BUY") 1 contract next bar at buyPrice stop; if shortTradesToday = 0 and marketPosition &lt;&gt;-1 then sell("SELL") 1 contract next bar at sellPrice stop; if high crosses above buyPrice then longTradesToday = longTradesToday + 1; if low crosses below sellPrice then shortTradesToday = shortTradesToday + 1; end; setExitOnClose; setStopContract; setStopLoss(dollarStop); Indicator Inserted Code inputs: expansionPIPS(.008); vars:buyPrice(0),sellPrice(0); If time crosses above Sess1EndTime then begin buyPrice = close - expansionPIPS; sellPrice = close + expansionPIPS; end; plot1(buyPrice); plot2(sellPrice); http://img99.imageshack.us/img99/573/erasierky9.jpg

--- 帖子 #774 ---
I have taken the profit target out of the system as it is damaging to the overall backtested results regardless of it's value. I generally disagree with any method of profit target as it has proven to be based on the biases and fears of the trader rather than commonsense ro statistics. You will find that most significant moves can continue in that direction for quite some time. It's a well known market truth that is exploited over and over again. Taking a profit when the market starts to rally is like saying "That's enough money" or "I am afraid that the market will snatch it back, so I will take my profit and run". Really you should be saying: "Gimme more of that"

--- 帖子 #775 ---
